Current Affairs Commentary

Address on the Opening Day of the National Vocational Education Conference

Taking advantage of the opening of this vocational and labor creation exhibition, the Ministry of Education convened the National Vocational Education Conference in the capital, which has attracted considerable attention from the nation. The conference is scheduled to begin today and close the day after tomorrow. Participants include vocational education experts and representatives from various institutions. The discussions will cover various issues related to vocational education administration and organization, as well as methods for promoting vocational education, implementing vocational guidance, and training vocational teachers. During the conference, the Vocational Education Design Committee of the Ministry of Education will also convene to discuss major plans.

Since the Second National Conference passed the "Determining the Trend of Educational Facilities Proposal" submitted by the National Government, the advocacy of vocational education has suddenly become lively again, far exceeding the situation in the eighth and ninth years of the Republic. Speaking only from the perspective of the Ministry of Education, there are detailed regulations for vocational schools and procedures for provinces and cities to promote vocational education, and teaching material outlines, curricula, and equipment summaries for various subjects in vocational schools have been promulgated. There are also outlines for the registration and training of vocational school teachers in various provinces and cities, and the proportion of vocational education in secondary school funding has been determined. In addition, sending commissioners to various provinces for on-site inspections and organizing vocational education design committees have also achieved considerable results.

However, the promotion of a cause requires not only a central driving force but also consideration of the surrounding environment and reliance on multi-faceted cooperation to achieve significant results. The most important key lies in grasping the fundamental direction. We cannot fail to recognize that the current social landscape is still filled with feudal ideas. The middle and upper classes mostly believe in the traditional concept of "orthodox background" and are unwilling to easily allow their children to study vocational skills or engage in practical production. Moreover, after graduating from six years of primary school or junior high school, most children prefer to continue their education unless their families are in financial difficulties, and they are unwilling to participate in low-level production work. As for general shops and factories, they adhere to old ways and do not seek improvement, preferring to maintain the old-fashioned apprenticeship system and not valuing new-style vocational education at all. The future of vocational education faces various obstacles, which is already dangerous, not to mention the lack of teachers, the simplicity of equipment, and the difficulty in finding employment for graduates. Therefore, while the government is enthusiastically promoting it, some people are worried and anxious, believing that the second total collapse of vocational education is not far away.

We also feel that in the past ten years or so, discussions on this issue have mostly focused on minor details and rarely grasped the fundamental direction. Originally, there are two views on vocational education. One is to regard occupation as the goal and education as the tool. The initial motivation for promoting vocational education in Europe and the United States was to use education as a tool for developing or obtaining an occupation. As a result, the content of vocational education is inevitably narrowed, causing it to lose its social nature. The other view is much more insightful. It believes that vocational education has two values. On the one hand, it uses education to prepare individuals for occupations, enabling people to find their place. On the other hand, it provides opportunities for education through occupations, making education richer and more meaningful. The former value emphasizes the occupation aspect, while the latter emphasizes the education aspect. Both should be considered simultaneously and should not be neglected. Otherwise, if those who run vocational education only want to use education as a tool to solve occupations, or use educational theories to create occupations, without knowing how to implement education in established occupations or study educational facilities in established production institutions, how can it not become school-style vocational education? Students trained by this kind of vocational education are only fit to be scholarly craftsmen, so how can they talk about direct production?

To obtain the first value mentioned above, it is necessary to pay attention to vocational guidance, ensuring that the special talents of the guided can be adapted to their social service. To obtain the second value, education must be integrated into the production environment. Training occupations in production is the truly direct vocational training. The purpose of "learning what is useful, using what is learned, work assisting learning, learning assisting work" can be naturally achieved. We dare to contribute this opinion on the opening day of the National Vocational Education Conference.

U.S. Air Force Prepares for Second Formation Flight

Shipbuilding Program Intensified

(Washington) While dozens of naval aircraft and more than a dozen warships are searching for the two Australian aviators in the waters off Hawaii, Secretary of the Navy Swanson announced that the Navy Air Corps' long-distance flight to Hawaii or the Philippines will still take place. He stated that this long-distance flight across the Pacific Ocean is related to the naval exercise to be held near the Aleutian Islands next summer and is therefore imperative. Although there are no concrete plans for this, the Navy Air Corps may conduct round-trip flights between the mainland and Alaska to the Hawaiian Islands as part of the naval exercise to be held near the Aleutian Islands in Alaska in July and August next year. After the fleet completes its exercise near Alaska, it may be preceded by naval aircraft and quickly head to Hawaii. Swanson stated that after the Navy Air Corps successfully flew from the mainland to Pearl Harbor last spring, the Navy Department began to consider this long-distance flight plan. Liaison flights between the U.S. mainland, Alaska, Hawaii, the Philippines, and other U.S. territories are necessary and proper exercises. The success of the formation flight last spring proves that naval aviators and naval aircraft are capable of this long-distance flight. Regarding general naval preparations, Swanson stated that the Navy Department has no intention of changing its plan to bring naval strength to the limits permitted by the treaty by 1942. Mr. Swanson further stated that naval experts, in view of Japan's possible abandonment of the treaty, are now considering ways to accelerate shipbuilding when necessary. (National Telegram on the 5th)

U.S. Reaffirms Maintaining Current Naval Ratio

Equality in Armaments Does Not Guarantee Equality in Security

Advocates for Sincere and Universal Reduction by the Three Nations

(London) When U.S. Chief Delegate Davis first announced the U.S. naval position today, he reaffirmed the U.S. government's advocacy of maintaining the naval balance of power stipulated in the Washington Naval Treaty. Mr. Davis stated that the alternative based on equality in armaments will not achieve equality in security. The United States agrees to gradual reductions. He has proposed, under the instruction of President Roosevelt, a sincere and universal reduction in naval armaments, which can be implemented without changing the comparative strength stipulated in the naval treaty and without endangering the security of participating countries. Because no compromise has been reached on the reduction, he has stated that we are still prepared to abide by the Washington Naval Treaty and continue the London Naval Treaty, with only minor modifications as required by the environment, in order to gain the enthusiastic support of the signatory countries. Mr. Davis also stated that once the principles in the 1922 treaty are abandoned, it will inevitably lead to instability, international suspicion, and wasteful competition, and no country will obtain true benefits. According to a Reuters correspondent in Washington, Americans view Davis's published remarks as a responsible expression of the U.S. government's views. This is the first official interpretation of the U.S. goals. President Roosevelt and Secretary of State Hull have not commented on this issue. Anyone who inquires is directed to Davis for answers. Although the United States' proposal for sincere and universal disarmament has never been formally announced, Secretary of the Navy Swanson has revealed that if Britain and Japan do the same, the United States may agree to reduce its navy by 20 percent or even higher. (Reuters Telegram on the 6th)

British-Japanese Talks Unfruitful

(London) Foreign Secretary Simon and Japanese Ambassador to Britain Matsudaira held talks again this morning at the Foreign Office. The content of the talks concerned the situation created after the Washington Treaty was soon to be declared abolished, and various solutions, such as whether the naval negotiations should be suspended or continued, and whether to convene a 1935 naval conference. It is generally believed that the talks did not result in any decisions. (Havas Telegram on the 6th)

It's Too Early to Talk About Adjournment

(Washington) News from London says that once Japan announces the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty, the United States will withdraw from the naval talks. Secretary of State Hull declared today that this news is premature, and that the U.S. naval delegation still hopes to establish an agreement to limit naval armaments. Since the talks are still ongoing and Japan has not formally expressed its intention to declare the abolition of the treaty, the U.S. naval delegation is still staying in London. (Havas Telegram on the 5th)

Italy's Refusal to Abolish Treaty is Fully Justified

Washington Treaties are Interrelated

Japan's Actions are Enemies of Peace

Rome The Labor Newspaper of the Fascist Party published an article explaining why Italy refused to simultaneously declare the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty with Japan. The article stated that Italy sees no reason to jointly declare the abolition of the treaty with Japan. Italy's ambition is to make its naval armaments equal to the most powerful country in Europe (referring to France). The Washington Naval Treaty stipulates that the tonnage of battleships and aircraft carriers for Italy and France is the same, so Italy's wish has already been partially realized. This is one of the reasons why Italy does not agree to abolish the treaty. Not only that, the Washington Naval Treaty is part of the entire series of treaties signed at the Washington Conference. (Note: Three treaties were concluded at the Washington Conference in 1921-22: one is the Naval Treaty with 24 articles, one is the Nine-Power Treaty with 9 articles, and one is the Four-Power Agreement with 4 articles. The latter was signed by Britain, the United States, France, and Japan, and its main purpose is to maintain general peace and maintain and respect the rights of each country in the Pacific region to all island territories, replacing the Anglo-Japanese Alliance of July 13, 1911.) No matter what Japan says, the Naval Treaty, the Nine-Power Treaty, and the Four-Power Agreement are interrelated and inseparable. If one is declared abolished, it is tantamount to declaring the abolition of the others. Therefore, from a constructive point of view, after the Washington Naval Treaty is declared abolished, the countries concerned must conclude a new agreement to replace it. Japan's unilateral action (referring to declaring the abolition of the treaty) is already enough to cause disputes. Moreover, although Italy is a great power, it is not as concerned about Pacific events as Britain and the United States. If Italy participates in Japan's actions, the result will only make international relations more chaotic. Italy's reasons for refusal are sufficient, as can be seen from this." (Havas Telegram on the 5th)

Germany Observes Progress of London Negotiations

Japan's Demand for Equality Indicates Ambitious Goals

Germany Cannot Remain Indifferent to Arms Expansion by Various Countries

(Berlin) The semi-official Political Foreign Correspondence Newspaper published an article commenting on Japan's imminent declaration of the abolition of the Washington Naval Treaty, stating that Germany's comments on the London naval talks are based on its position as an "objective observer." "Japan's naval demands are not only for unrestricted equality of rights, as Germany demands for arms issues, but also for its naval armaments to be equal to other countries in terms of quantity. Japan's argument is based on its island nation status and the political situation in the Far East. However, the United States has always believed that this argument is not sufficient." The newspaper concluded, "Once the issue of the ratio of naval forces in European countries becomes acute, Germany cannot ignore it and remain indifferent." (Havas Telegram on the 5th)

Britain's Far East Policy Cannot Hesitate

Lord Lothian Worries About World Crisis

Scrapping of Naval Treaty Will Affect Europe

Hopes the United States Will Join Collective Peace System

(London) Lord Lothian declared in the House of Lords today, "We are now gradually reaching the most critical stage in world history. The most far-reaching consequences depend on the policies that the British government will implement in the Far East in the next three to six months. There is no doubt that one of the signatories of the Washington Naval Treaty intends to announce the abolition of the treaty before the end of this year. If Britain upholds the principles of the treaty, the United States will definitely be our backer. However, we want to know to what extent the United States will maintain these principles. Russia and China can also be our supporters. China looks to Britain for help more than any other country. As for the other signatory countries, they can also unite and give their support from afar. If diplomatic power cannot succeed in the Far East and one country can tear up treaties, who knows if another country will tear up the Treaty of Versailles in the future? If so, the world will have another great war. But if we can uphold the neutrality of the Pacific, we can break down the biggest obstacle to the collective system, which is the United States' failure to join this system." Undersecretary of State Stanhope replied on behalf of the government, "We do not want to discuss the Far East issue now. The talks between the three major powers are currently underway. If we discuss this issue now, it will harm the collective peace system." (Reuters Telegram on the 5th)

British Naval Veteran Advocates Maintaining Maritime Supremacy

Free Construction of Cruisers

National Defense Ensures Security

British Navy to Undergo Major Expansion

(London) Lord Beatty, former Commander-in-Chief of the British Navy during the European War, delivered a speech at Queen's Hall tonight, expressing his regret again for the lack of British cruisers, saying, "What I am worried about is not the naval equality that Japan is demanding, because if the Japanese need equality, they must pay a considerable price for it. What I am worried about is that Britain must have seventy cruisers to be sufficient. Now, the task of seventy ships is being entrusted to fifty ships (the limit allowed by the London Naval Treaty). This is a serious mistake. I dare to tell you that if the naval conference can be convened next year, this error should be remedied at the conference so that Britain will not accept restrictions again and endanger its own security. In other words, we should freely build cruisers to match the special responsibilities we bear. This is possible. Some say that building warships costs a lot, and the British Navy Department must consider whether it has the financial resources. The answer is that other countries spend more on their navies than Britain, especially the United States. Why should our country not have these financial resources? Maintaining naval strength is of great importance to the British Empire. The government must be aware of this, and we must also fulfill our responsibilities. Once maritime hegemony is lost, there is no hope of recovery. History is full of precedents. We must be careful." (Havas Telegram on the 5th) (London) The Daily Telegraph reported that the number of British naval soldiers and officers will be greatly expanded, and the budget for next year will take this into account. The newspaper continued that although the British Navy occupies an important position in the world, it is not as good as other countries' navies in terms of personnel numbers, so there is a need to increase it. This move has nothing to do with the results of the naval talks. (Havas Telegram on the 5th)

Saito Promotes in the United States

Boston Japanese Ambassador to the United States Saito stated at a banquet of the Japan Society today that Japan is prepared to reduce its navy by half, but only if Britain and the United States follow suit. After the Washington Naval Treaty is abolished, Japan does not want an era not governed by treaties, but hopes for a more reasonable international agreement. Japan will not make a challenge to compete in building warships, but hopes for an active reduction in naval armaments. Soviet Union Recruits Red Army

Peasants and Workers Eagerly Enlist

TASS Moscow, November 3 The Soviet Red Army is recruiting young people born in 1912 this year. This recruitment work is now actively underway. The majority of recruits are shock workers from factories and collective farms. Recruits in the Moscow region are all literate. Most of them have passed shooting and "Ready for Labor and Defense" badge examinations. The day of conscription each year is like a holiday. Strong young people are recruited into the army. Their joy is like entering school. The general public is extremely concerned about the recruits. Their comrades often line up to send them to the registration office. Factory managers, collective farm managers, and local Soviet chairmen often accompany them. Families also eagerly hope for their conscription, because their joining the Red Army has no hindrance to their families. (Since the phenomenon of unemployment has been eliminated, their old mothers and others have no worries about no one taking care of them when their children enlist.) One day, the workers of the Baku Himitto Factory gathered in the room of shock worker Kagramanov. Mr. Kagramanov said to them, "Today, the elder and second sons of my family are joining the Red Army. They are doing very well in their studies and are both shock workers in the factory. I hope they will become shock soldiers in the Red Army and outstanding defenders of our great motherland." The streets and squares near the recruitment office are decorated with flags, slogans, etc. Government commissioners, senior Red Army officers, Soviet heroes, famous artists, and writers often visit these recruitment offices. They sometimes give speeches or perform in front of the public. The development of Soviet industry has greatly changed the social composition of the Red Army. 45 percent of the Red Army soldiers are now industrial workers, and 42.5 percent are peasants (70 percent of whom are collective farmers). About half of the Red Army members are Communist Party members and Communist Youth League members.

Organizing International Troops to Maintain Order During the Saar Plebiscite

The French Foreign Minister's Proposal Endorsed by Britain and Italy

The League of Nations Passes the Saar Report

(Geneva) The proposal made by French Foreign Minister Laval to maintain order in the Saar region with international troops has been endorsed today by the League of Nations representatives of Britain and Italy. British Lord Privy Seal Eden and Italian representative Baron Aloisi both announced that they were prepared to send troops to the Saar next year during the plebiscite to maintain order and protect Saar residents from retaliation. The League of Nations Council will reconvene at 6:30 PM today. The Council has officially filed the French Foreign Minister's plan and requested the Saar Commission to report in detail on its feasibility before the end of this session. As for preventing Saar residents from retaliation after the vote, the foreign ministers of both Germany and France have declared guarantees. (5th, Kokumin News Agency)

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council unanimously passed the Saar report today. Beforehand, French Foreign Minister Laval and Soviet Foreign Minister Litvinov declared that if the plebiscite held on January 13 next year results in the Saar people wanting to maintain the status quo, then the Saar residents can vote again on whether or not to merge with Germany. As for Laval's proposal to maintain order in the Saar with international troops, it has been endorsed by Britain and Poland. (6th, Kokumin News Agency)

(Geneva) At today's meeting, the League of Nations Council unanimously passed the Saar Three-Person Committee's report on handling difficulties in the plebiscite. Each member of the Council shook hands with and congratulated Aloisi, the chairman of the Three-Person Committee, and others. British representative Eden stated that the agreement reached in Rome a few days ago was a good omen for relations between France and Germany, as well as among Western European countries. Czech Foreign Minister Dr. Piniès stated that this agreement has eased tensions between the countries involved.

It is widely expected that after the Council passes this report, the British Parliament of the Saar Committee will immediately proceed with the plan to organize international police to maintain order during the plebiscite. According to general opinion, about 1,500 to 2,000 police officers would be sufficient, to be organized from soldiers selected from the British, Belgian, and Italian armies. It is said that the Netherlands has also been asked to participate, and it is likely that the Netherlands will agree. Although there are rumors that a country in the Scandinavian Peninsula will also be asked to participate, it is widely believed that this police force will be composed of people from the above three or four countries. The moral authority of this army is very important. This will be the second international army organized under the authority of the League of Nations. The first international army previously handled the dispute between Colombia and Peru in South America. The Three-Person Committee's report mentions several important events. As for the question of how to define the situation established under the Treaty of Versailles, it is also discussed in the report. What is now clear on this point is that the League of Nations has the right to order a second plebiscite if necessary. The General Assembly report advocates that if the status quo remains unchanged, residents can acquire Saar citizenship, but Saar people of German ethnicity can freely change their citizenship to German. The report states that Saar residents without voting rights also have the same protections as voters. The documents exchanged between the foreign ministers of France and Germany, proving this guarantee, are also attached to the report. (6th, Reuters)

British Conditions for Participation

(Geneva) Britain has decided to participate in the international action to maintain order in the Saar during the plebiscite, but on the condition that France and Germany approve this resolution. The above news was announced today by British Lord Privy Seal Eden at the League of Nations Council meeting. The public paid great attention to this news, as this decision by Britain contributes more to peace than any other action. Eden stated that while both sides have great goodwill, he acknowledged that there may inevitably be some incitement and disturbances during and around the time of the vote. Rather than remedying the situation afterwards, it is better to prevent it beforehand. Before Eden spoke, French Foreign Minister Laval stated that to show that France has no ulterior motives, France does not want to participate in the organization of the international police force, but asks the League of Nations to be responsible for maintaining order. This proposal by France is on the condition that Germany also does not participate in the international police force. Russian Foreign Minister Litvinov said that he must consult with Moscow before deciding whether or not to participate. The British and German governments have formally welcomed Britain's proposal to maintain order during the Saar plebiscite, considering it a great contribution to European peace. At the same time, the League of Nations Saar Three-Person Committee is currently considering the issue of the international police force, feeling that this matter should not be borne by Britain alone. Therefore, it is planned that Britain, Belgium, the Netherlands, Switzerland, and Luxembourg will jointly organize the police force. The League of Nations generally expects a tense period after the plebiscite. (5th, Reuters)

Exploring Germany's Stance

(Geneva, Saar District)

Aloisi, the chairman of the Three-Person Committee, visited German Consul General Krall in Geneva, asking Krall to prove the German government's stance on the entry of international police into the Saar. (5th, Kokumin News Agency)

(Geneva) According to German sources here, Germany will not accept the proposal to send international troops to maintain order in the Saar, at least until it has been discussed. (5th, Havas)

(Berlin) Yesterday, it was learned that the Council was holding a meeting to discuss the Saar plebiscite, at which French Foreign Minister Laval requested the organization of international troops to be sent to the Saar region to maintain order, but for the sake of impartiality, the French were willing to abstain from participating in this army. According to informed German sources, it is believed that Germany will not oppose the dispatch of an international police force when necessary to maintain order in the Saar. Although Germany still believes that there is no reason to dispatch special troops, because France is willing to abstain from participating in this international army, Germany considers it a generous act and is quite satisfied. Regarding the composition of this international army, Germany has raised some reservations, arguing that only neutral countries should participate, and that countries related to either the French or German parties should not participate. Germany considers the Czech Republic, Belgium, Lithuania, and the Soviet Union to have closer ties with France and should not participate. From France's perspective, it may also be believed that the Free City of Danzig and Austria are less qualified to participate in this international army. (6th, Havas)

The Three-Person Committee's Report on the Saar Question

The Content is Divided into Two Major Parts

Both Politics and Economics are Discussed

(Geneva) The Saar Three-Person Committee submitted a report to the League of Nations, divided into two major parts. The first part details key points, such as the interpretation and scope of the agreement, the nationality and options of residents, the extension of protections to the non-electorate, the treatment of residents after the establishment of a new situation, social security, and the status of Saar officials. The second part pertains to financial and coal mine issues. The report also includes correspondence between the Three-Person Committee and the French and German governments, the rights that the Saar people should receive after merging with Germany in the future, and the agreements between Germany and France on financial issues. The report first explains the current situation, largely as presented in the July 31, 1934, memorandum of Barthou. The report states that, according to the provisions of the Treaty of Versailles, if the results of the popular vote favor maintaining the status quo, the League of Nations will not continue to be the guardian of the Saar region, but the League of Nations will exercise its governing power and try to safeguard the interests of the residents and create a permanent situation. The report strictly adheres to the provisions of the peace treaty, so there is no indication of a second vote. Regarding nationality, Saar residents of German nationality will acquire Saar nationality after voting, but may choose to be German nationals. People of non-German nationality will maintain their original nationality, but may choose to be Saar nationals. For the non-electorate, both the German and French governments assume the same obligations, namely that neither party shall abuse or discriminate against those who have resided in the Saar region for the past three years, regardless of their political views. All disputes must be submitted to the Permanent Court of Justice in The Hague. No government may prevent anyone who wishes to leave the Saar, nor may it prohibit them from selling their property. Both governments also guarantee individual social security. In addition, a large portion of the report describes financial issues and the agreements made by the German and French governments in Rome. The full text of the agreement is also attached to the report, stating that if the Saar is to be merged with Germany in the future, France will cede all mining rights to Germany after receiving a payment of 900 million francs. The method of payment is also specified, one of which is to be calculated in coal units. In addition, there are other trivial matters, such as French loans and investments, and the currency system. (5th, Kokumin News Agency)

Responsibility for the Marseille Incident Included on the Agenda for this Session

(Geneva) The League of Nations Council held a closed meeting and, without discussion, unanimously decided to include the Yugoslav application on the agenda for the mid-term of this extraordinary session. The Yugoslav application originally requested the League of Nations Council to discuss the Marseille incident at the next session in order to investigate the responsibility for the crime. Yugoslavia's Expulsion of Beggars Causes Tensions in Central Europe to Increase

Kirov's Body Cremated, Soviet Russia Executes Sixty-Six People

(Moscow) Before Kirov's cremation today, Soviet Russia executed sixty-six terrorists and conspirators. Thirty-seven people were executed in Leningrad, and twenty-nine people were executed in Moscow. A few hours later, Kirov's body was cremated. The high number of executions in one day is the first since the Great Revolution. Nominally, they are not related to Kirov's assassination, as most of these people had already been sentenced to death by military tribunals and the Soviet Supreme Court. Most of these people entered the country from Poland, Latvia, and Finland. However, outsiders generally believe that this mass execution is the Communist Party's response to the anti-Soviet terrorist movement. These people had already been sentenced to death, but the executions had been delayed. Soviet party officials seized the opportunity today to order simultaneous executions before Kirov's cremation. (5th, Kokumin News Agency)

(Moscow) On the 5th, the Military Collegium of the Soviet Supreme Court secretly tried 39 criminals who were preparing and organizing the assassination of Soviet officials. The court proved that most of these criminals came from Latvia, and some came from Finland and Poland. Their task was to organize terrorist activities. Based on the provisions of the Criminal Procedure Code and the order issued by the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union on December 1, the Military Collegium sentenced 37 of them to death and confiscated all their property. The remaining two will be further investigated. Those sentenced to death have already been executed. On the same day, the Military Collegium of the Soviet Supreme Court secretly tried 32 criminals with the same charges in Moscow. The court proved that most of the criminals came from Poland, and some came from Finland. Their purpose was to organize terrorist activities. Based on the provisions of the Criminal Procedure Code and the order issued by the Central Executive Committee of the Soviet Union on December 1, the Military Collegium sentenced 29 of the criminals to death and confiscated all their property. The remaining three will be further interrogated. Those sentenced to death have already been executed. (6th, TASS)

(Moscow) Kirov's body is still lying in state in the Trade Union Hall. Yesterday afternoon, a large number of workers went to pay their respects, and it did not stop until 10:00 PM. A large crowd stood waiting regardless of the cold weather and heavy snow to enter the hall to pay their final respects, including workers, scientists, schoolchildren, and women with young children. The number of wreaths in the hall continued to increase. Friends of the deceased, party workers, factory workers, scientists, artists, authors, Red Army soldiers and officers, sailors, aviators, etc., took turns standing guard by the coffin. The honor guard was replaced every five minutes. Delegations from all over the Soviet Union are arriving one after another, sending wreaths. In these few hours, more than 1.2 million people passed through the hall to pay their respects. At 10:00 PM, the paying of respects ceased. At this time, members of the Party Central Committee, government officials, and representatives of various republics gathered in the hall, listening quietly to the mourning music. At 10:55 PM, Stalin, Molotov, Kaganovich, Voroshilov, Ordzhonikidze, Mikoyan, Chubar, Postyshev, Petrovsky, and Yezhov served as the last shift of the honor guard. At 11:40 PM, Kirov's body was cremated in front of members of the Central Committee and government officials, the Leningrad and other delegations, and the deceased's relatives. (6th, TASS)

DuPont Company Supplied Zhang Zuolin with Ammunition

(Washington) The Senate Munitions Investigating Committee today involved the DuPont Company's arms transactions with Chinese government officials, with further startling discoveries based on the DuPont Company's confidential documents. These documents were obtained by the Senate Committee and announced this morning. Senator Clark read a confidential letter from Gilis, the DuPont Company's manager in China, to Gause, the company's foreign salesperson, stating that the arms embargo against China had long been abandoned, and the Inspector General of Customs also admitted that this was the reality. The letter, dated July 31, 1924, was related to Zhang Zuolin, stating that the Chinese government was willing to incur high debts in order to satisfy its desire for war. Clark accused the DuPont Company of shipping the arms it sold to China to neutral ports to evade the arms embargo. DuPont did not admit this. Gause of the company claimed that trade with China was very strong. In 1924, 40 tons of gunpowder were smuggled into China and delivered to the Sino-Japanese Trading Company. Although the gunpowder was well-protected, it was still obtained by a certain warlord in Fengtian. In a letter from Gilis to Gause on March 28, 1925, it was stated that 20 tons of gunpowder were sold to the Sino-Japanese Trading Company and eventually shipped to Zhang Zuolin's Fengtian Arsenal. This was an open violation of the arms embargo by the Japanese authorities. In addition, a Norwegian company directly sold 150 tons and 300 tons of gunpowder to Zhang Zuolin, and an Italian company sold 16,000 rifles and 28 million bullets to the Northeastern warlord. Shanghai Stock Exchange Brokers Petition for Reduction or Exemption of Transaction Tax

(Nanjing) The Shanghai Stock Exchange Council and brokers, because the Ministry of Finance has levied a transaction tax, fear that it will affect market operations and increase the burden. In addition to the Council holding meetings to discuss, the brokers have also decided to entrust the Council to petition the central government for reduction or exemption. Gu Xinyi and Mu Ouchu were sent to Nanjing on the 6th as representatives to petition for exemption. Gu said that the Stock Exchange and brokers hope that this tax will not be implemented to avoid increasing the burden on merchants and reducing market operations, or they hope that the tax rate will be reduced to lighten the burden. According to the current transaction tax rate, an average transaction of 10,000 yuan, considering both the buyer and the seller, is taxed at three yuan. They requested that the heads of the various Stock Exchange councils be invited to attend the review by the Finance and Commercial Law groups of the Legislative Yuan so that they can express their opinions. Regarding the future participation in the review committee of the Legislative Yuan, the government seems to be easing its stance. (6th, Special Dispatch)

Investigation of Postal Services in the Capital

(Nanjing) Sources from the transportation sector reveal that Nanjing's postal services have been declining year by year due to the development of radio communications. However, there has been a slight increase in ordinary parcel and local mail. A recent survey of the past year's postal services shows: (1) A total of 1,086,210 registered mail items were handled last year, a decrease of more than 37,000 items compared to previous years. (2) A total of 695,740 express mail items were handled, a decrease of more than 27,000 items compared to previous years. (3) A total of 4,166,790 ordinary mail items were handled, an increase of 150,000 items compared to previous years. (4) 600 insured letters were handled, a decrease of 920 items compared to previous years. (5) A total of 525,050 local mail items were handled, an increase of 56,000 items compared to previous years. (6) A total of 153,610 airmail items were handled, a decrease of 55,000 items compared to previous years. (7) A total of 65,770 parcel post items were handled, an increase of 7,300 items compared to previous years. (8) The value of postal remittances in silver dollars was 5,746,610 yuan, a decrease of one million yuan compared to previous years. (9) The value of postal drafts in silver dollars was 2,068,480 yuan, a decrease of more than one million yuan compared to previous years. (10) Fifty postal telegrams were transferred, a decrease of 40 items compared to previous years. (11) Three hundred and forty sealed letters were sent by private bureaus, a decrease of more than one hundred items compared to previous years. (Special dispatch from the 6th)

Gu Zhutong and Jiang Dingwen came to the province a few days ago for the distribution of troops in the pacification zone, the liaison for clearing out bandits on the Jiangxi-Fujian border, and the implementation of post-disaster relief, have all been discussed and meticulously planned. Jiang Dingwen returned to Longyan by military plane three days ago accompanied by Counselor Zhang Jianwu and more than ten attendants, riding in three military planes. Gu also went to Nanjing on the same day with Chen Cheng to report everything to Chairman Chiang. The Fujian Pacification Headquarters was established in Longyan on the first day, and moved into Zhangzhou immediately. The Jiangxi Pacification Headquarters had already been prepared in Ji'an. Gu also telegraphed on the first day to take office. The bandit areas of Jiangxi and Fujian are adjacent and intertwined, and the junction of Lichuan, Guangchang, Shicheng, Ruijin, and Tai'ning, Jian'ning, Ninghua, and Tingzhou, where scattered bandits appear and disappear. It is still necessary to cooperate to suppress them. Therefore, Jiangxi and Fujian are jointly divided into twelve pacification zones, with eight zones in Jiangxi and four zones in Fujian. The commanders of each zone have also been announced. Chen Jicheng in northwest Jiangxi, Tan Daoyuan in west Jiangxi, Yu Hanmou and Xiang Hanping in southern Jiangxi, Zhao Guantao in northeast Jiangxi, Sun Lianzhong and Zhang Fang on the east bank of the Gan River, and Luo Zhuoying on the Jiangxi-Fujian border. The original commanders of the various columns concurrently serve in the northwest and southwest of Fujian. The Pacification Commanders of each zone have unified control and command over the troops, teams, and baojia within the zone. The administrative commissioners and county magistrates in the jurisdiction are also under their supervision, in order to coordinate the clearing of the countryside, post-disaster relief, disaster relief, construction, and restoration. (December 3)

Hankou Chamber of Commerce Repeatedly Telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to Strive for Freedom of Cash Transportation

The Jianghan Customs Detains Cash, Please Return It Quickly

Hankou Correspondence, Hankou's financial situation previously caused great disturbance due to the Ministry of Finance's restriction on cash transportation to Hubei. The Chamber of Commerce has telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to strive for freedom. In recent days, cash imports have slightly improved, and the situation is slightly better. The commercial sector is fortunate to be able to turn around. However, a Wuhan business previously transported cash to Hankou, but was suddenly detained by the Jianghan Customs, causing another twist. The business community believes that Hankou is the most important commercial center in central China, connecting the north and south. If this case is not resolved, the city's commerce will inevitably decline and go bankrupt. Therefore, on the 5th, they telegraphed the Ministry of Finance again to strive for freedom of cash transportation and requested that the Jianghan Customs be ordered to quickly return the detained cash. The telegram stated that cash should circulate as a principle, and if there is any obstruction, the financial market will inevitably be chaotic. For example, after the autumn harvest in Hubei Province, local products enter the market, and farmers are used to transacting in cash. At this time, the use of cash, in particular, requires flexible turnover. Wuxue is an important town in the lower reaches of Hubei Province and is also a cotton-producing area with very complex commercial exchanges with Hankou. The fact that cash transported to Hankou has been detained means that Hankou merchants must carry cash to that place to purchase cotton, which will inevitably lead to the inability to export. Furthermore, the transportation of goods to various counties and cities to purchase local goods, as well as the transportation of cash from various counties and cities to Hankou, cannot be free. If cash cannot circulate freely within the province and local products cannot be listed on the market, life will be extremely difficult and there will be no way to adjust the situation. How can rural areas be rescued and the market prospered? This financial reorganization policy is inevitably unsustainable and without a source. The association feels that this is dangerous and dares not remain silent. Therefore, we specially urge the ministry to investigate and approve and to quickly seek relief. For the circulation of cash within Hubei Province, we request that free transportation be permitted. If it is necessary to prevent abuses, the cash transported from Hankou to various counties and cities should be allowed to apply for a passport at the Jianghan Customs. The cash transported from various counties and cities to Hankou or from Hankou to various counties and cities should be certified by the local Chamber of Commerce in order to ensure smooth flow and rescue agriculture and commerce. At the same time, we request that the provincial government forward a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, approving the requested justification, and ordering the military and police agencies along the land and water routes, as well as various tax collection bureaus, to inspect and release all cash transferred within the province, without any obstruction, in order to provide relief and avoid panic. (5th)

Yantai Market Suddenly Experiences Great Panic

--Treacherous Merchants Transport Silver to Dalian--

--Creating a Major Crisis in the Market--

--Jinan's Finance Is Also Tense--

Jinan Correspondence, Jinan's financial market has always been quite stable, but unexpectedly, an unprecedented storm has occurred in Yantai. Since the increase in the price of silver, a large amount of silver has been exported from various places. Yantai and Dalian are only separated by a strip of water, and transportation is extremely convenient. Recently, every thousand yuan of silver transported to Dalian can earn more than eighty yuan. A group of treacherous merchants, who only seek profit, have been secretly transporting silver there. Although the Finance Department previously restricted the export of silver, each person could carry no more than two hundred yuan. However, the treacherous merchants are making large profits from smuggling and are hiring people to carry silver out of the country on their behalf, with subsidies of three yuan or less per two hundred yuan. After deducting expenses, they still have a profit of forty or fifty yuan for every thousand yuan transported. Later, the Finance Department changed the limit to no more than fifty yuan per person, and then to twenty yuan. However, the treacherous merchants are still making large profits and continue to smuggle silver. Since so much silver has been exported, the Yantai market has been completely empty, creating an unprecedented panic in the financial world, and economic turnover is sluggish. Since last Friday (30th), all transactions in cloth have completely stopped, and people are in a state of panic. The Yantai Chamber of Commerce and Zhang Kuiwen, the Yantai Special Zone Administrative Commissioner and concurrently Director of the Public Security Bureau, have summoned the China, Communications, and Minsheng Banks in Yantai to discuss emergency measures. They decided that each bank should issue banknotes as much as possible to circulate in the market, but they felt that there was a severe shortage of silver, and they planned to temporarily suspend cash redemption to maintain the status quo. When the news reached Jinan, the Finance Department and the Minsheng, Communications, and China Banks believed that the method of suspending cash redemption was inappropriate. They decided to issue banknotes as much as possible and to transport a large amount of silver to Yantai for normal cash redemption to provide relief. On the 2nd, Wang Xiangrong, Director of the Finance Department, summoned Song Fuqi, Deputy Manager of Minsheng Bank, Chen Junren, Manager of China Bank, and Guo Weibai, Deputy Manager of Communications Bank, to discuss ways to rescue Yantai's finances. They decided that on the one hand, the Finance Department would issue an order to absolutely prohibit the export of silver, and on the other hand, each bank would transport silver to Yantai to maintain the situation and issue more banknotes. In the past two days, Minsheng, Communications, and China Banks have transported hundreds of thousands of yuan in silver to Yantai, and they will continue to transport silver according to the needs of the area. The Finance Department also summoned the managers of various banks and major silver houses on the afternoon of the 3rd to discuss measures.

Furthermore, Jinan's banks, seeing that there is a shortage of silver everywhere, especially in Yantai, are not only allocating cash from Jinan to rescue Yantai, but also issuing banknotes in Jinan. Fearing a run on the banks, they are collecting cash to prepare for unexpected events. On the one hand, they are transferring three to four million yuan in cash from Shanghai, and on the other hand, they are tightening the market in Jinan and extracting cash from various silver houses. As a result, the market has suddenly become tight. Shanghai drafts have fallen from 13 yuan per thousand on the 3rd to 18 yuan on the 4th, a drop of 5 yuan. Shanghai telegraphic transfers have fallen from 7 yuan per thousand on the 3rd to 3 yuan on the 4th, a drop of 6 yuan. As for lending, everyone is wary and dares not lend much. Interest rates have soared. On the 3rd, the rate for one and a half months was 1.6%, and the rate for two months was 1.7%. On the 4th, the rate rose to 1.7% for one and a half months and 1.75% for two months. (4th)

Northwest Inspection Diary by Our Special Correspondent, Geng Ya

The Terrifying Encounter After Passing Xingxingxia

At 1:00 PM on the 13th, we departed from Malianjing. We encountered a blue-black desert for about twenty li. To the northwest, the Xingxingxia mountain range rose and fell intermittently, with alternating dark and bright sunlight. The vast expanse of misty waters created ever-changing, eerie reflections, a scene truly unlike anything in the interior. After another ten li, we saw several circles of ruined foundations and a short stele, marking the Jiaoya Gou, the boundary between Gansu and Xinjiang. After passing this point, dusk had already fallen, and a crescent moon hung askew. We traveled over undulating terrain for about thirty li before reaching a place with lush grass and abundant water, where we camped for the night. The day's journey was over sixty li, about ten li from Xingxingxia Station. There were over ten wells at the campsite, and water could be drawn with a bucket only three or four feet deep. Unfortunately, only one well had sweet water; the rest contained alkali and saltpeter, which even the camels wouldn't drink.

After setting up camp and preparing tea, one of the camel drivers returned from gathering firewood, exclaiming in alarm, "I saw a light in the distance, gradually moving towards our tents. I fear it's not a friendly presence! What should we do?" The escort team originally consisted of seven men, but because the Xingxingxia and Shiban Jing stations lacked grass and fodder, it was inconvenient to permanently station troops. In the morning, five men had been left to guard Malianjing, and the remaining two, soldiers from Han Lianfu's troops, were specially assigned to escort us out of the gorge. Upon hearing the camel driver's warning, they immediately grabbed their rifles and went outside to investigate. After circling the tents, they found no light at all. They then asked the camel driver to lead them back to the original spot. Looking in the same direction, the bright light reappeared as before. However, after careful observation, they realized the light was not approaching from afar but shining through a hole in the top of the tent. They suddenly realized it was a case of being scared by one's own shadow, and everyone burst into laughter.

We set off the next morning. The red willow and white thorn bushes stretched endlessly, interspersed with spike-shaped pink flowers, which were particularly lovely. Sadly, the harsh cold of the frontier meant that ice and snow would arrive early, and this autumn scenery would soon wither. After ten li, we entered the gorge. Initially, the road forked, but here it converged into a single path. The sturdy grass and branches along the roadside were covered with clumps of cotton, which, if collected, would easily amount to dozens of catties. This was because cotton merchants transported the cotton from Turpan and Hami. As they passed through the gorge and exited, the small donkeys, upon seeing the grassland, raced ahead, causing the bags to break and the cotton to spill out. At the entrance to the gorge, the ridges and peaks were interwoven, with countless piles of stones stacked on top. There are three possible explanations for their formation: (1) Ma Zhongying's first entry into Xinjiang, when retreating through the gorge after a defeat, fearing an attack by pursuing troops, dug a long trench and erected black stones to create a feigned force. This occurred in 1931. (2) In the desolate wilderness of the desert, loose soil and open fields are easily swept away by wind and sandstorms. Therefore, stone piles were built in advance as markers, similar to the Mongolian "Obo." (3) Superstitious travelers often pile stones to resemble pagodas, praying for good fortune. If they stand for a long time without falling, they are particularly pleased. The stone piles related to explanations (2) and (3) were commonly seen during our journey. However, when they were first created is unknown.

The gorge is a dry sandy riverbed, overgrown with Malian grass. The pods burst when ripe, resembling orchids. On both sides, the cliffs rise thousands of feet, steep and terrifying. Erosion from wind and rain has created holes as large as mortars. Six or seven blockhouses have been built on top, and two or three barracks have been constructed below, clearly demonstrating its military importance. The gorge station used to have twenty or thirty households, all of which were destroyed and burned, with none intact. The three temples—the Temple of Guan Yu, the Hall of Guanyin, and the Jade Emperor Pavilion—were built according to the mountain's terrain and were originally magnificent and imposing. Now, they are covered in mud and debris. A lonely postal worker resides in the temple, his thoughts unknown as he lives with the dim lamp and ancient Buddhas. It is said that the gorge produces stones that shimmer like starlight, and ten li from the gorge, there is a Xingxing Dong (Star Cave), hence the name Xingxingxia. However, the construction records of the Jade Emperor Pavilion and Xinjiang gazetteers refer to it as Xingxingxia. Ultimately, it remains to be verified who is right and wrong, or whether both names are equally acceptable.

Near Xingxing Dong, there are many crystal stones. Several columns grow from a single base, and people from Anxi often dig them up and plant them in wooden vessels to enjoy their beauty. The crystals sparkle and gleam, dazzling the eyes. In another Temple of Guan Yu, three or four li outside the gorge, it is said that there used to be two large crystals, each two feet square, but they were sadly destroyed in the fire along with the temple. Behind the temple, there is a steep stone path carved by hand. A stone tablet stands in front of the temple, warning people to be careful. After descending the stone path, we traveled along the sandy riverbed, turning from north to west for over twenty li. The high mountains on either side of the river were naturally steep and treacherous. The mountains were devoid of vegetation and mostly composed of sandy cliffs. Yellow, white, red, and black colors distinguished the peaks. Looking ahead, the mountains seemed to pierce the sky, like bamboo shoots emerging after rain. The road ahead was vast and invisible. Some say that the jagged black mountains are outcrops of coal, but this is not true.

The reporter dismounted and walked, examining the shiny stones. I was thinking that in such a desolate place, in times of war, one man could hold off ten thousand. Suddenly, I heard a faint shout of "Stop! Stop!" Looking back, I saw Akim running towards me, shouting, "Three riders armed with guns have been spotted at the small fork in the road to the right and rear!" Upon hearing this, Han Lianfu and Ma's soldiers immediately threw off their old sheepskin robes, which they had been wearing on horseback, onto the ground. They quickly loaded their rifles and prepared to fire. The camel train also stopped ringing its bells and halted. Akim rode out alone to inquire. The three riders also approached, and then from the direction of Xingxingxia, where the dust was rising, over ten riders shouted and galloped towards us. Behind them, the glint of guns was faintly visible. Han Lianfu glanced at the cliffs on either side, his face turning pale, as if asking himself, "What can be done?" He quietly told the reporter to "crouch down." At that moment, Akim waved his hand, shouting, "Come, come, come!" The reporter followed Han Ma and went towards him. The ten or so riders who had come later also galloped up and surrounded us. Some had wispy beards, others had long, mixed white beards. Some wore long robes like Mongolians, while others wore Zhongshan suits and military uniforms with Qing Tian Bai Ri (Blue Sky with a White Sun) emblems on their hats. In total, there were fourteen riders. After Akim introduced them, we learned that they were the garrison troops sent by Yao Lebos, the garrison commander of Hami and Zhenxi, to escort us.

We immediately dismounted, exchanged greetings, and took photos to commemorate the occasion. They then took the reins and galloped ahead, quickly disappearing into the distance. Initially, Commander Yao had received a telegram from Anxi's Regiment Commander Ma, stating that Xingxingxia fell within his garrison's jurisdiction, so he had also sent troops to escort us. These troops were eager to meet us quickly and took a shortcut, almost completely missing us if not for the three riders coming from behind. The local custom of the garrison troops is to shave their heads but not their beards. Thus, although the soldiers had the appearance of "Old General Huang Zhong," their spirit of galloping and shooting was no less impressive than that of young men. Among them, the Long Tong Shui Ka (Company Commander), "Togutman," and the Company Commander "Tunlan Kele," along with three or four others, were knowledgeable, spoke fluent Chinese, and were available for consultation. Their hospitality was especially appreciated. In the evening, we arrived at Shitou Jingzi (also known as Xiaohong Liuyuan), a journey of sixty li. We set up camp and cooked dinner. The garrison troops had arrived earlier and were staying in a dilapidated Temple of Guan Yu. They also came to our tents one after another. Initially, they let the reporter sit in the central position at the rear of the tent, facing the entrance. To the left were Han Lianfu's soldiers from Anxi, Akim and others, in the host position. To the right were Company Commander Tunlan Kele, Commander Togutman, and the other garrison troops, in the guest position. Whether host or guest, everyone sat in a circle around the brick tea stove burning camel dung in the center of the ground. Those who wanted to leave the tent would walk in front of people, to the left or right, but never behind. The two pillars supporting the tent and the stove in the center were in a straight line, forming the boundary between the left and right sides. Those who passed between the stove and the rear pillar (the front pillar near the entrance was not restricted), or deliberately made noise with the fire tongs, or only held one end of the pot ear and dragged it on the ground, or placed their chopsticks on the bowl after eating instead of handing them to the "Zhua Guo (cook)" for washing, were all considered to have violated the rules and were fined. The "Zhang Gui (boss)" was fined double. These tent rules were somewhat similar to those of a Mongolian yurt.

That night, we met the garrison troops for the first time and had interesting conversations. The reporter had not learned the local language, so direct conversation was difficult. Those who could speak Chinese seemed shy and did not speak much. Akim acted as an "interpreter," and we were able to begin our pleasant conversation. The reporter said, "I deeply admire you gentlemen for coming so far to escort us. When we reach a more populated area, you will be rewarded." Akim immediately translated this, and they repeatedly said "Hash (meaning 'yes')" incessantly. Then, they all raised their hands to express their gratitude and replied, "We came here to welcome you on orders. We set off in a hurry and didn't even have time to bring any Hami melons. We also didn't manage to hunt any yellow sheep or wild horses along the way. We are very sorry." The reporter said again, "I am very grateful for your protection." They replied, "You and we are all sons born of the same father. We are here to protect you, which is like brothers protecting brothers. Moreover, this is our duty as people who receive rations. There is no need for thanks. However, the photo we took when we met today probably didn't turn out well. We would like to tidy up our uniforms and take another one." The reporter nodded in agreement, saying, "Marching in the Gobi Desert makes it difficult to be too meticulous. Moreover, you are wearing the Qing Tian Bai Ri emblem on your military caps, which is identical to those used by the Central Army, giving people the best impression." After eating hand-grabbed rice, only the company commander and commander stayed in the tent, while the other brothers returned to the dilapidated temple, each sleeping in their saddles.

Suzhou Sojourners from Huzhou Organize Opera Performance to Raise Disaster Relief Funds

This year, the six counties of Huzhou suffered severe drought and disaster. People from Huzhou residing in Shanghai organized a disaster relief committee to raise funds. Now, Bao Diexian, Yao Tongsun, and Chen Aishi, Shen Lianfang, and Shen Tianxin, members of the Huzhou Disaster Relief Committee in Suzhou, have initiated a request to renowned Kunqu opera artists from Suzhou and Shanghai to perform Kunqu opera for three days at the Kaiming Theater in Suzhou's North Bureau, from the 7th to the 9th of this month, to sell tickets and raise disaster relief funds. Renowned Kunqu opera artists from Shanghai, including Wang Xiaofan, Xu Junyun, Pan Xiangshan, Xu Ziquan, Xu Shaojiu, Zhao Xingshu, Yin Zhenyi, Zhao Zenghe, Jing Gu Zhuren, Qiu Ying Zhaizhu, and Miss Shen, are all on the list of invitees. The programs for all three days are very exciting. Today, Chen Aishi, Shen Tianxin, Ling Songru, Pan Runsheng, and Bao Xiaodie have already traveled to Suzhou to arrange everything. It is said that Yao Tongsheng and Bao Diexian are responsible for the preliminary negotiations in Suzhou. When the time comes, the people of Jin Chang will not only be able to enjoy the elegant music but also rescue the disaster victims. The scene of busy traffic should be a grand one.

Songjiang Police Inspector Resigns to Take Another Position

Mr. Yan Jishi, the police inspector of this county's Public Security Bureau, has recently accepted an invitation from his friend Zhang Hanwei, the former police inspector of the Provincial Department of Civil Affairs and the current director of the Wuxian Public Security Bureau, to take a position. Mr. Yan has therefore requested his resignation from Director He in order to take up his new post in Suzhou.

An Unexpected Turn in the Wuxi Girl's Suicide Case

Zhou Yufen, a girl from Hexiang Bridge in Jiangyin County (namely the maidservant of Dr. Zhu Daji's family), committed suicide by taking poison in room 43 of the Park Hotel the day before. Because the poison was so potent, she was taken to the Brothers Hospital for treatment, but it was ineffective, and she died from the poison that evening. The next day, Zhou's mother, Qu, and her sisters, Yuying and Bao, heard the news and came to Wuxi from Cheng. They wailed loudly at the Dongmenwai Hostel Public Office, which was heartbreaking to those who heard it. However, because of their poverty, they had no money for a coffin, so they went to Dr. Zhu Daji's house at No. 40 Dalou Lane to beg for help. To their surprise, the Zhu family not only refused but also scolded Zhou's mother harshly, beat her, and accused her of colluding with the teahouse waiter, Tan Genda, to extort money, resulting in her being taken to the Public Security First Branch Bureau. After questioning by Bureau Member Fan, Zhou Yuying, the sister of the deceased, stated that her sister, Zhou Yufen, was a maidservant in Dr. Zhu Daji's family, and this suicide was caused by a relationship with Zhu Daji, as stated in her suicide note. According to Zhu Daji, the suicide of Zhou Yufen had nothing to do with him, and Zhou's mother came to borrow coffin money, which was tantamount to extortion. After obtaining the confessions, Bureau Member Fan considered the case to be serious and immediately prepared a document to transfer it to the General Bureau, which will then transfer it to the local branch court for trial.

The Manager of Qinchang Silk Factory Flees with the Funds

The Qinchang Silk Factory in Tieshu Bridge outside the South Gate was opened by Chen Yinglong, a silk merchant from Shanghai, and Ding Qinsheng, a local resident. The factory has been in operation for less than two months. The factory's silk was usually sold in Shanghai by the manager, Chen Yinglong. However, Chen had ulterior motives and recently absconded with all the silk funds, avoiding seeing anyone. This caused the factory's finances to become strained. The assistant manager, Ding Qinsheng, also fled a few days ago because he found it difficult to maintain the factory. As a result, the factory was forced to shut down, owing more than twenty days' wages to the female workers and more than a month's salary to the staff. Currently, staff members Pan Helin, Wei Xiufang, and Pu Yinhuan have impounded and stored the factory's remaining cocoons. They have also published a notice to inform Assistant Manager Ding to come forward to handle the situation so that it can be resolved.

A Major Fire in Xiaomeng Lake, Zhenjiang

The house of Widow Shen (also known as Shen Siliumao) in Loudong Lane, Xiaomeng Lake, Zhenjiang, caught fire last night (5th) at around 6:00 PM due to carelessness while preparing dinner. At that time, the north wind was piercing, and the thatched and tile houses were densely packed together. The lanes were narrow, and the god of fire unleashed his rage. Soon, the fire spread to the neighbors. Fire brigades from various sections rushed to the scene and fought hard to extinguish the flames. However, because the lanes were narrow and the roads were rugged, fire engines could not enter, and the lack of water made it even more difficult to extinguish the fire. The county party headquarters commissioned Bu Yulin and Yan Deshen, the owner of Loudong Park, to extinguish the fire. Their residences were also reduced to ashes. The fire was gradually extinguished at around 8:00 PM, having destroyed more than twenty tile and thatched houses, resulting in significant losses.

Anti-Japanese Hero Jiang Minsheng Arrives in Zhenjiang

Major General Jiang Minsheng, an anti-Japanese hero from the Northeast Volunteer Army, is currently traveling around giving lectures on the tragic situation in various parts of the Northeast to arouse the attention of the Chinese people. Yesterday, he arrived in Zhenjiang from Dandong and is staying at Room 9 of the City Hotel. He plans to stay in Zhenjiang for a week before going to Nanjing. He plans to audit the Fifth National Congress and then go to Anhui and Jiangxi, followed by Hunan, Sichuan, Hubei, and other provinces. He expects his trip to take a year. After completing his lectures in the above provinces, he will return to Shanghai and then travel from Shanghai to Fujian, Guangdong, Guangxi, and other provinces. He also plans to go to various parts of Southeast Asia.

Nantong Encircles and Suppresses Qin Gang's Bandits

Ten bandit ships with more than two hundred bandits have been discovered at the Qin Gang estuary in Lusi. The Nantong Maritime Public Security Team went to suppress them on the evening of the 4th. The coastal area has been unusually cold for days, with rain and snow. The Baoshan District Department, fearing that the bandit ships would flee, has telegraphed the Yanshui Maritime Public Security Team to rush to the area for encirclement and suppression.

Zhu Shusheng to Visit and Inspect Nantong

Zhu Shusheng, the president of the High Court, is scheduled to visit Nantong on the 10th to inspect the court, the Fourth Prison, and the detention center. After completing his official business in Nantong, he will proceed to Rugao.

A Major Fire in Wangjiaba, North of the City

A major fire broke out in Wangjiaba, north of the city, on the evening of the 5th. The fire brigade fought to extinguish the fire for two hours, destroying five or six homes and causing significant losses.

Jiangyin Patrol Officer Arrests Gamblers, Villagers Riot

There were crowds gambling at the Zhangjia Teahouse and Wangjia Tea Garden in Yunting Town, east of the city. On the 3rd, the Public Security Bureau sent Patrol Officer Zhang Zhendong with more than twenty police officers to arrest them. They arrived in Yunting around 6:00 PM in the afternoon. They caught more than ten people playing mahjong on the spot, as well as thirty or forty others shaking dice and drinking tea. Patrol Officer Zhang, without distinguishing between right and wrong, wanted to search everyone present, which aroused public anger. For a time, there was a great clamor, and the crowd began to shout and hit the police. The patrol officers fired two warning shots into the air, which further incited the crowd. The gamblers were protected and escorted out of the teahouse. Later, the town's merchant corps came to maintain order and asked the teahouse owner to sign a bond at the town office. Patrol Officer Zhang then led the police back to the city and reported the matter to Director Liu.

Fire in Hangzhou on a Winter Night, Four Die

Ge Yongkang, a farmer from Liubao Township, outside Taiping Gate in Hangzhou, was from Xiaoshan and made a living growing vegetables and fruits. His wife, Chen, had three children: the eldest daughter, Hehua, was six years old, his son, Bingyan, was four years old, and his youngest son, Xiaomao, was only one year old. Last night at 7:00 PM, because it was cold, his wife and children went to sleep first. Ge went out, but accidentally left a fire near the wood pile. In an instant, the thatched house caught fire, and the fire spread rapidly. His wife and children were trapped by the smoke and flames and could not escape. They were all buried in the fire. When Ge heard the news and rushed back, he saw his family of four with their heads and faces charred, a tragic sight. The police station reported the incident to the court, and the coroner performed an examination the next morning before the bodies were placed in coffins.

Tailor Kills Apprentice

Yan Agou, the owner of the Huachang Tailor Shop on Xinmin Road in Hangzhou, had a violent temper. A few days ago, he severely beat his apprentice, Luo Shunbao, with a wooden stick over a minor matter, causing serious injuries. Afterwards, he was stingy with medical expenses, so the apprentice died because he did not get proper treatment. The father of the deceased, Luo Xiangwu, reported the incident to the court for an examination and accused Yan of causing death by injury, requesting that he be punished and compensated.

Local News

Preparatory Committee for Victory Celebration Distributes Notices for Motorcade Parade

All Sectors of the City to Hang Flags on the 10th to Celebrate

The Preparatory Committee for the Victory Over the Communist Bandits Celebration Conference organized by all sectors of the city has decided to hold the conference at 10:00 AM on the 10th (Sunday) in the auditorium of the City Chamber of Commerce. A motorcade parade will be held at 2:00 PM. It is reported that the Preparatory Committee, to ensure that all sectors understand the motorcade parade arrangements, has printed and distributed a motorcade parade notice to participating organizations and groups. Party and government agencies will jointly issue a notice to all people's organizations in the city, requesting them to send representatives to participate in the celebration conference. The following is a record of the Preparatory Committee's situation:

——Motorcade————Parade Notice——

The Preparatory Committee issued a notice yesterday regarding the motorcade parade, which is recorded below: 1. Date: December 10th, 2:00 PM; 2. Assembly Location: Ximen Heping Road; 3. Assembly Time: 1:00 PM; 4. Route: Heping Road, Nanyang Bridge, Milu Road, Fangbang Bridge turn, Minguo Road, Xiaodongmen turn, Bund, Guan Bridge, Xuejiabang turn, Hujunying, Guohuo Road, Chezhan Road, Xiaoximen turn, Zhonghua Road, Dananmen, Xiaodongmen turn, Fangbang Road, Temple Front, Fangbang Road, Laoximen, Heping Road disband; 5. Yang Yongtai Discusses the Imminent Eradication of Communist Bandits

Sichuan Province's Bandit Suppression Measures Finalized

Nanchang Headquarters Will Not Be Moved for the Time Being

Yang Yongtai, Secretary-General of the Bandit Suppression Headquarters for the Three Provinces, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing the day before yesterday to attend to personal matters. Yesterday morning, Mr. Yang received visiting reporters at his residence. According to him, the banditry in Jiangxi Province is being completely eliminated through relentless encirclement and suppression. The remaining Communist bandits in the four provinces of Hubei, Henan, Anhui, and Jiangxi number less than 100,000, with about 40,000 to 50,000 of them roaming outside. Only half of these remaining bandits have guns, the rest are unarmed, and their strength is extremely weak. It is expected that they can all be eradicated within six months. Communist banditry in Sichuan Province has gradually spread in recent years. The reason for this is that the troops in the province lack coordination. Recently, Liu Xiang, the Commander-in-Chief of Bandit Suppression in Sichuan Province, repeatedly met with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in Beijing to seek instructions on bandit suppression. Measures have been taken to reorganize the troops in Sichuan Province, and the military operations for bandit suppression in Sichuan Province can proceed smoothly hereafter. Regarding the relocation of the Bandit Suppression Headquarters for the Three Provinces, Mr. Yang stated that it is too early to discuss this. Although the Communist bandits in Jiangxi Province are about to be eradicated, the local vitality has not been restored, and it is inevitable that some petty thieves will remain in hiding and disrupt public order. Therefore, the headquarters still needs to handle other political work. However, if necessary in the future, it may be moved to Sichuan Province. Mr. Yang further stated that he accompanied Chairman Chiang Kai-shek on an inspection tour of various places in North China. He was very impressed along the way. North China is quite calm now, and local order is gradually becoming peaceful. As for the rumors that he will go north to preside over political and diplomatic affairs, they are absolutely inaccurate. Moreover, Huang Yingbai was originally appointed as the Minister of the Interior as a concurrent position, and he himself will not leave Beiping. Mr. Yang concluded by saying that the New Life Movement is being promoted extensively in various places. This is the ancient Chinese morality that has been neglected by the Chinese people in recent years, leading to near extinction. He earnestly hopes that the Chinese people will quickly rise up and promote it.

US Senate Philippine Investigation Group Returned to the Country on the Original Ship Yesterday

Inspecting the Commercial Situation of the Philippine Ports

The Reality of Japanese Dumping in the Philippines

According to Shen Shi News Agency, the five-member US Senate Philippine Investigation Group arrived in Shanghai on the Canadian Empress yesterday. Yesterday afternoon, they attended a banquet hosted by the US Consul General, Keninghan, and visited various places in the afternoon. At 7:00 last night, they took the original ship to the Philippines for investigation. The details are as follows:

Pre-Departure Interview

Before boarding the ship, reporters interviewed the investigation group. Most of them kept their mouths shut and remained silent. Then, one of the members told the reporter that they are going to the Philippines to investigate the commercial situation of the Philippines. The US government is now paying close attention to the interests of the Japanese in the Philippines. The Philippines is about to become independent and organize an autonomous republic. The US government will pay more attention to the actions of the Japanese in the Philippines in the future.

Organization Process

According to the organization of the Philippine Investigation Group, after the Philippine Parliament passed the Philippine Independence Act last year, it proposed to the US Senate to organize an investigation group to go to the Philippines to investigate the commercial changes in the region after independence. The proposal was approved by the US Congress last summer. Then, Senator Ellison Hayden went to the Philippines in August to conduct a preliminary investigation before returning to the country to report.

Investigation Purpose

It is reported that the US Congress is now most concerned about the Philippine sugar industry, because the Japanese have been dumping in the Philippines recently, which has greatly affected Philippine sugar, and business has plummeted. In addition, the group will also discuss measures to deal with the dumping of Japanese goods in the Philippines and issues such as "preferential tariffs."

Investigation Personnel

The investigation group has a total of five people, including Senate Senators McTudor (California), Miller (Maryland), McLane (Tennessee), Chipson (Washington), and the captain of the US Marine Corps in China, Baimeng, accompanied them to the Philippines.
