Page 12

Salt Affairs Audit Office Streamlines National Salt Affairs

—— Draft Opinion on Controlling the Salt Industry ——

—— Continuous Study and Contribution Accepted by the Ministry of Finance ——

According to New Voice News Agency, the Salt Affairs Audit Office has completed the streamlining of national salt affairs and has drafted an opinion on controlling the salt industry. Director Zhu, Transport Officer Miao, and Auditor Yao have been studying it in Shanghai for days and will contribute it to the Ministry of Finance for adoption and implementation. The reporter of New Voice News Agency has obtained the streamlining process and the research and control situation, which are recorded as follows:

Streamlining Field Production

The Salt Affairs Audit Office was established in January of the second year of the Republic of China, originally established to improve salt administration, streamline tax revenue, and unify national salt affairs, centralizing power in the central government. It is divided into four periods: (1) the start-up period, from the second to the sixth year of the Republic of China; (2) the organizational completion period, from the seventh to the twelfth year of the Republic of China; (3) the period of interference by local authorities, from the thirteenth to the seventeenth year of the Republic of China; and (4) the recovery and streamlining period, from the eighteenth to the twenty-second year of the Republic of China. Streamlining is now complete. Streamlining field production and managing the storage of salt are the most important tasks for consolidating tax revenue. Therefore, the first step in streamlining field production is to build assembly mounds and concentrate salt storage for management. In the past, the General Office proposed building large-scale salt mounds in the Changlu area as a model for each area. Subsequently, official warehouses were built in the Furongdong Field in southern Sichuan, which merchants and residents still find convenient today. In February of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, in imitation of Changlu, it was decided to start with northern Huai. Today, the Huai North Salt Mound has been completed, and salt warehouses have been built on the four banks of the Yangtze River. Zhejiang, Songjiang, Fujian, Guangdong, and Shandong are all preparing to build salt mounds in imitation of the Huai North model. However, in Changlu, during the forty-something years of the Republic of China, the anti-smuggling camps were extremely corrupt, and the field was leaking private salt, which could not be investigated or prohibited. Due to the failure to effectively manage the field production, even with good salt mounds, smuggling could not be prevented. Now that administrative affairs are also handled, the construction of salt mounds and the streamlining of anti-smuggling efforts are carried out at the same time, which is twice as effective and has achieved great results. Therefore, private salt in northern Huai is now sharply reduced, and tax revenue is increasing daily. Although it is due to the large amount of sales, it is also closely related to the field production management method. The source of private salt is entirely in the field. If the field does not leak private salt, how can there be any private salt? In the future, when the mound projects in Fujian, Guangdong, Zhejiang, Songjiang, Shandong, and other areas are completed, the results will be considerable.

Streamlining Transportation and Sales

The transportation of salt is the pivot of salt production and sales. If there is production, there must be sales. Merchants and vendors must pay taxes before transporting salt for sale and are allowed to pay with promissory notes. Therefore, transportation and sales are the root of excise tax. The more salt is sold, the more tax revenue increases. China's salt trade is bound by the system of licenses. The transportation and sale of salt are not free, which greatly hinders the streamlining of salt affairs. After the establishment of the Audit Office, it first advocated improving the transportation system. The first important point is to abolish the exclusive merchants and allow the people to trade freely. From the third year of the Republic of China to the eighth or ninth year of the Republic of China, the areas where licenses were opened included the northern Huai, Sichuan, Guangdong, Fujian, and Shanxi areas, and a part of Changlu. At that time, the results were quite considerable, but unfortunately, the political situation was unstable, and some areas changed back. The destruction in Sichuan and Fujian was particularly severe. The improvement of transportation and sales should be absolutely free. If progress is too rapid, it will inevitably cause resentment. The Audit Office has always been based on gradual progress in reform matters. At present, a transitional method is temporarily adopted. In August of the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, the contracted merchants in eastern Zhejiang, Wenzhou, and Chu were abolished, and free trade was implemented. After the opening, as of the end of this year, the tax revenue collected in five months totaled more than 583,000 yuan, an increase of more than 159,000 yuan compared with the tax revenue before the opening. In March of the twenty-second year of the Republic of China, the exclusive merchants in the four counties of Lin, Tan, Fei, and Yi in Shandong were abolished, and free trade was restored. All transportation and sales in the four counties were changed to free areas. As for the four banks of the Yangtze River, which have always been known as corrupt, in April of the twenty-second year of the Republic of China, it was agreed that the Huai salt on the four banks, whether in the field or on the shore, should be at the highest standard of the current set price, and merchants should be allowed to freely reduce prices under the standard legal price to compete for sales. As for the former four banks of southern Huai, which were known as the twelfth Wei as the corrupt den, the Huai salt transported to the Wei was usually under the jurisdiction of the Transport Envoy. During the eleventh year of the Republic of China, the Northern Huai Sub-Office Manager consulted with the Tuizhou Sub-Office on the rotation of transport on the four banks, but the Transport Envoy of both Huai strongly opposed it, and it was not implemented. Now, the promotion of direct rotation of transport has achieved significant results. Most of the salt is directly transported from the Huai North production area to the shore, while the salt transported from the twelfth Wei is still transported by sail. Now, a method is being sought to abolish sail transport. However, merchants, boat owners, and dock laborers are all people who eat corruption. The streamlining of salt affairs was originally to eliminate corruption, and the Yang General Station should be abolished. How can sail transport be retained? The fundamental streamlining should still improve the transportation system and gradually proceed to prepare for the implementation of new laws.

Streamlining Tax Rates

Streamlining tax rates. In the early years of the Republic of China, the tax rates were chaotic and there were many types. After the establishment of the Audit Office, the improvement of salt tax began with the elimination of all kinds of tax items and unified them. In October of the second year of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Finance promulgated the Salt Tax Regulations and stipulated uniform weights and measures for tax collection and weighing of salt. Before the promulgation of the statutory weights and measures, the national salt affairs temporarily used the Sima scale as the weight and measure. These regulations stipulated that salt tax should be levied per dan, with a tax of 2.5 yuan per 100 jin, and stated that it was for temporary use. Once the Salt Law was promulgated, it would be stopped. In the seventh year of the Republic of China, the Salt Tax Regulations were revised again, with a tax of 3 yuan per dan. However, the conditions in each region were different, and uniform taxation throughout the country was difficult to implement. However, in the third and fourth years of the Republic of China, the new tax was implemented. Although the four banks of the Yangtze River and the Yunnan area failed to follow the Salt Tax Regulations, with each dan exceeding 4 yuan or exceeding 3 yuan, the audit side advocated tax before salt, eliminating the malpractice of tax arrears from the past, which was indeed effective. However, since the fifth year of the Republic of China, military affairs have frequently arisen, and various provinces have added surcharges in addition to the regular tax to raise funds. The tax rates in various regions have become uneven again. Now that we are streamlining, all low-tax areas are raised, and high-tax areas are gradually reduced. The various local and central surcharges are numerous and difficult to assess, and have been consolidated. All field taxes paid in the production area and the central surcharge are collectively called the regular tax. The shore tax paid in the sales area and the central surcharge are collectively called the sales tax. The local surcharge is collectively called the surcharge. Salt tax revenue must be compared with sales volume. In recent five years, tax revenue has been increasing, and the heavy tax rate is one reason, and the sales volume is also very important. China's population is said to be 400 million or more. The total sales volume of salt should reach more than 50 million dan. If private salt can be eliminated, tax revenue will definitely increase without increasing taxes. Therefore, we must strengthen the management of field production, streamline anti-smuggling efforts, and work hard to combine the symptoms and the root cause. In the future, private salt can be reduced. Then, the low-tax salt can be increased, and uniform taxation throughout the country will definitely be achieved. The implementation of the new law should be used as the beginning of this.

Streamlining Anti-Smuggling

In the Qing Dynasty, the salt affairs agencies did not have formal salt patrols. Only the Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces had salt-catching camps, patrolling the Taihu Lake and Yangzhou areas, under the jurisdiction of the Governor-General of Liangjiang and the Governor of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. All commanders and leaders were recruited from salt smugglers. The patrolmen in each production and sales area were mostly recruited by merchants themselves, called merchant patrols. These salt patrols were nothing more than organs for various exclusive merchants to smuggle. In the early years of the Republic of China, anti-smuggling camps were established. Later, field police were established in the field area, all under the jurisdiction of the Transport Envoy or Deputy Transport Envoy and the Salt Transport Bureau. In the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, an anti-smuggling office was established within the Ministry of Finance, and anti-smuggling bureaus were established in various regions, while the field police were still under the administrative agencies. In the eighteenth year, the anti-smuggling bureaus were changed back to the jurisdiction of the Transport Envoy, Deputy Transport Envoy, and Salt Transport Bureau. It was not until March of the twentieth year that the Ministry of Finance submitted a request to the Executive Yuan, which was submitted to the State Council for discussion and resolution, to change the anti-smuggling teams and field police in the provinces to the jurisdiction of the audit agencies. The handover was carried out by various regions in April and May. After taking over, the anti-smuggling teams were changed to tax police, and the camp system was changed to a district system. Tax police sections were established in the various sub-offices and audit offices, or in the tax collection bureaus, and were directly commanded by the managers of the sub-offices and the auditors of the audit offices. The candidates for section chiefs, district chiefs, and team leaders were all selected and appointed by the General Office. All officers and police, from officers to police officers, were issued personal certificates with photos, stating the year and month of arrival, experience, and guarantors to prevent fraud. Tax police officer training centers were established in various regions to ensure that everyone can fulfill their duties and abide by discipline. By comparing the sales of salt in recent years, the effectiveness of streamlining anti-smuggling can be proved.

Eliminating Malpractices

Malpractices are illicit gains, one being customary regulations, also known as regulation fees. The accumulation of abuses in salt affairs is the worst of these. For more than ten years, no one has reformed them. In the twenty-first year of the Republic of China, the administrative agencies were changed to be concurrently held by the audit side. Since taking over, the biggest abuse in the administrative aspect has been the acceptance of malpractices. It has been practiced for a long time and is taken for granted. Those who offer bribes consider it an obligation, and those who receive them regard it as a right. Greed has become a trend, and they are not ashamed. How can salt affairs not be bad? To seek the integrity of administration, the elimination of malpractices must be an urgent task. Therefore, the General Office strictly ordered all regions to fundamentally eliminate all kinds of malpractices. All concurrently appointed personnel were able to be honest and law-abiding and strictly prohibited all items of malpractices. Thus, the accumulation of hundreds of years of abuses was completely eliminated, which was a major innovation in salt affairs.

Planned Control

After the Salt Affairs Inspection Office completes the reorganization of national salt affairs, it plans to implement unified control of the national salt industry. Miao Qiujie, the Salt Transport Commissioner of Lianghuai, has already drafted an opinion paper. For days, Zhu Tingqi, the Director of the Salt Affairs Inspection Office, Yao Yuanlun, the Inspector of Hubei Bank, and Miao Qiujie, the Salt Transport Commissioner of Lianghuai, have been studying the opinion paper at the Shanghai Inspection Office. A decision will be made to submit it to the Ministry of Finance for adoption and implementation upon completion of the study. It is believed that this unified control opinion, once adopted and implemented by the Ministry of Finance, will genuinely benefit salt merchants and also increase national tax revenue.

China Merchants Sze Hai Line Decides to Employ Chinese Citizens as Staff

Striving for Equal Status Based on Treaty

Rather Abandon Passengers Going to Hong Kong

The Hong Kong government requested that the China Merchants Bureau use foreign captains, chief officers, and chief engineers for the Sze Hai Line in order to obtain a passenger license. The Bureau believes this is an insult to the nation and difficult to comply with. It has already submitted a request to the Ministry, stating that Chinese crew members have already been issued licenses by the government, that the Hong Kong government has no right to examine them, and should not refuse to issue passenger licenses. The details are as follows:

Temporarily Employing Foreigners: When the Hai Yuan arrived in Hong Kong on its first voyage, it already had Hong Kong passengers on board. When applying for a passenger license from the Hong Kong Marine Department, the department ordered that the chief officer also be a foreigner. At the time, there was no alternative but to temporarily hire a foreigner, V. Reinburg, in Hong Kong to serve as chief officer, but only for one trip. The original chief officer, Chen Bangda, was not dismissed and was still asked to stay on board to serve. A foreigner will not be used as chief officer on the next voyage.

Abandoning Hong Kong Passengers: The Bureau has already appointed Ma Jiajun as captain of the Hai Ting and will also appoint Teng Shibiao as captain of the Hai Li, which will arrive in Shanghai soon. The senior crew members on the Sze Hai Line will definitely be Chinese citizens. It would rather not sell tickets to Hong Kong passengers. If the Hai Yuan Line insists on using a foreigner as chief officer, it is willing to abandon Hong Kong passengers and not take them on board, and will determine a solution after future negotiations with the government.

Certificates are Valid: The China Merchants Bureau has now submitted a report to the Ministry of Communications, stating that China has joined the International Convention for the Safety of Life at Sea and has already obtained equal status in international navigation. All crew licenses issued by the Chinese government should be recognized by all countries, and the Hong Kong government has no right to examine Chinese crew members. This matter concerns international status and should be fought to the end. Before a resolution is reached, Hong Kong passengers will not be carried temporarily. The Hai Heng Sets Sail: The Hai Heng is scheduled to sail to the Jinliyuan Wharf this Saturday. It will officially clear customs next Tuesday and begin its maiden voyage to Lianyungang on Wednesday. Director Qian of the Longhai Railway Bureau has telegraphed the Bureau that there will be a grand welcoming ceremony when the ship arrives. The Railway Bureau will also present generous gifts to the Hai Heng, and order 300 servings of tea and refreshments to entertain visitors.

After exporting, legitimate merchants transporting silver should obtain passports. However, the passport application procedure should be the responsibility of the Chamber of Commerce to guarantee before prompt issuance to meet needs, or follow the method of transshipment of gold, with the Chamber of Commerce guaranteeing transport to Customs. Zheng Zenan, an executive committee member and chief of the finance section, has been specially dispatched to Beijing to negotiate with the Ministry of Finance. It is reported that Mr. Zheng left for Beijing last night.

Dragon Mountain Ship Owner Summoned by Japanese Navy

Occasional Shelter

Should be Understood and Released

The San Bei Company's Dragon Mountain ship, traveling from Shanghai to Saigon to transport foreign rice, encountered a storm en route. It has escaped danger, as reported in this newspaper. Unexpectedly, the ship anchored off the coast of Taiwan to pump water and repair the ship due to water entering the front hold. Because it mistakenly stopped in a naval area, a dispute occurred, leading to the ship's owner, Lao Guan, being summoned by the Japanese navy. Yesterday afternoon, Shanghai received a telegram from the ship detailing the situation, as follows:

Encountering Wind and Water

The Dragon Mountain ship is slightly larger

than the Mount Tai. This

time, it departed from Shanghai to Annan Saigon

to transport a large quantity of foreign rice to Shanghai. On the third

day of this month, the ship encountered a hurricane at sea south of Sheshan. The ship's owner, Reisby, fought against the violent waves. Due to the surging waves, seawater poured over the ship's hull, causing the front hold of the ship to be

completely flooded. In the emergency, a rescue signal was sent. Fortunately, the hurricane passed, and the Dragon Mountain ship was able to move forward. However, due to the water entering the ship, they urgently sought to pump it out to ensure safety.

Dispute Over Stopping the Ship

When the Dragon Mountain ship advanced to the Taiwan sea area, the owner deemed that the seawater entering the front hold had exceeded the water

line, making navigation very dangerous. He chose a safer place to anchor and ordered all crew members to carry out the work of pumping water and repairing the parts of the ship damaged by the huge waves. Unexpectedly, the location where the Dragon Mountain stopped was within the Japanese naval area stationed in Taiwan, where commercial ships were not allowed to anchor. The Dragon Mountain ship was not initially aware of this, so soon after stopping, a Japanese warship sailed over to watch the Dragon Mountain ship, causing a major dispute.

Stating the Circumstances

The Dragon Mountain ship's captain, Reisby, and the ship's chief engineer, were summoned for questioning by the Taiwan Japanese Naval Headquarters.

Reisby and others then took a Japanese warship to the Japanese fleet headquarters in Taiwan, giving a detailed account of the reason for the Dragon Mountain ship's anchoring there, with no other intention. The facts are clear and can be investigated. However, the Dragon Mountain is still anchored there.

Should Be Released

Yesterday afternoon, after the San Bei Company received a wireless report from the Dragon Mountain ship's chief officer, as of yesterday, the owner and others had not returned to the ship. The work of pumping the water that entered the front hold had been carried out. The water in the front hold has now been pumped out, and the water in the rear hold is still being pumped. According to the crew's speculation, given this special situation, the Japanese naval department will surely understand and release them.

Lumber Association Advocates Domestically Produced Fir

Declaration Aims to Save the Nation and Merchants

The city's Lumber Association, after repeatedly requesting the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward a request to the Executive Yuan's Ministry of Industry, ordering all public and private construction projects in various provinces and cities to use domestic fir wood, has been approved. Starting from January 1st of next year, it will announce and implement the minimum standard for the use of domestic fir wood, taking into account the construction conditions in various places. It is now known that the Lumber Trade Association, in order to actively promote it, in addition to making every effort to research the supply and design needs, issued a declaration to save the nation and merchants. The declaration is copied as follows:

Since ancient times, our country has always used domestic fir wood for building materials. Moreover, domestic fir wood is strong and durable, and many buildings have stood firm and upright for hundreds of years. Looking at the ancient temples and pagodas of the world, they have undergone several dynasties and are still worthy of admiration and viewing. Although half of it is due to the hard work of the craftsmen in designing, the firmness and durability of fir wood is the main reason. After the establishment of commercial treaties, imported foreign pine was sold in the market, and fir wood was abandoned. Our industry has been hit by this until now, and it is almost in a desperate situation. The durability of foreign pine is far less than that of domestic fir wood, but it is not used in construction, causing tens of millions of dollars to flow out of the country every year, which is very painful. The flooding of foreign pine is a small harm to this industry, but a great harm to the entire country. Wandering day and night without a solution, this association had previously requested the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to forward a request to the Yuan and ministries, ordering the subordinate provincial and municipal engineering organs to implement the use of domestic fir wood as building materials, to save the country and merchants. A reply was received, approving the implementation from January 1st of the 24th year. The Municipal Bureau of Engineering has also posted a notice, outlining two minimum standards for the use of domestic fir wood. Now that the notice has been issued, it is bound to be implemented. In addition to notifying all colleagues in the industry to collect as much as possible for purchase by all sectors, this association will make every effort to study the needs of the design and will publish it in the Shen Bao and Xin Bao newspapers to promote it and save the right to benefit. Currently, the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce is compiling a book to revitalize industry and promote domestic goods, soliciting interviews from all public officials. We colleagues are confined to a corner and have very little experience. We have already sent letters to the lumber associations of Hankou, Nanjing, Hangzhou, Changzhou, Wenzhou, and Fujian to inquire about detailed information, hoping to gather wisdom and benefit. I think there is no shortage of industry veterans and enthusiasts who promote domestic wood in the country. I hope to have your guidance, which I will appreciate greatly.

Four Members of the Communist Assassination Squad Sentenced to Death

Kuang Huian, Zhao Xuan, Meng Huating, and Zhu Jinming All Sentenced to Death

Lin Ermei Sentenced to Three Years Imprisonment, Tang Wanxuan and Others Acquitted

After the Communist bandits' assassination squad was uncovered by the police, Kuang Huian and other important members of the squad were prosecuted by the police to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu Higher Court for repeatedly committing assassination crimes. The hearing has concluded, and a ruling is pending. The previous reports have repeatedly stated the details. Yesterday afternoon, the sentencing date arrived. Zhao, Wu, and Zhou, the three judges, together with Prosecutor Zhong, ascended the seat and ordered the ten defendants, male and female, including Kuang, to be brought forward. After a few brief questions, the verdict was announced. Kuang Huian and Zhao Xuan were each sentenced to 15 years of imprisonment for the crime of forming a group with the aim of endangering the Republic of China. Each was sentenced to death for three counts of premeditated murder, and all were to be executed together. Meng Huating and Zhu Jinming committed one fewer murder than Kuang and Zhao, so they were also sentenced to death together. Lin Ermei was sentenced to three years of imprisonment for possessing military firearms and ammunition, and the firearms and ammunition were confiscated. Tang Wanxuan, Li Yangshi, Li Zhoushi, Liu Jinrong, and Zhang Lishi were all acquitted. After the verdict was announced, Attorney Zhan Jifeng, the legal advisor of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, requested that all ten people be allowed to be taken to the Public Security Bureau for investigation and then returned for execution after the investigation. The Third Branch of the Higher Court also sent personnel to court to request the transfer. The police lawyer, Gan Jingxian, and Prosecutor Zhong, stated that if the acquitted defendants were taken away and no suspicion of committing a crime was found, they requested that the Bureau be ordered to return them quickly for release. After deliberation by the court, it was approved to hand them over to the Public Security Bureau for investigation and then return them immediately so that the Third Branch of the Higher Court could be notified to transfer them.

Round-the-World Feat of Polish School Ship

Can Arrive in Shanghai in Mid-March Next Year

The Polish school ship Pomerania, a giant three-masted sailing ship with several large sails, is also equipped with modern motor machinery inside, but it relies entirely on wind power when sailing, and the motor is kept in reserve and not used. The ship has all kinds of equipment, carrying a total of 106 officers and sailors, and 61 naval school students. It set sail from Gdynia, Poland in September, passing through the Panama Canal, Japan, Shanghai, the Suez Canal, and North Africa, etc., for a round-the-world voyage. This is the first time a Polish ship has made this feat, as the ship was donated by the people of Pomerania Province, Poland, hence the name Pomerania. According to news from the Polish Embassy in this city yesterday, the ship is scheduled to dock in Yokohama, Japan, for one or two days, and then in Nagasaki for a week for repairs, and then sail to Shanghai, arriving around mid-March next spring. The Polish community in Shanghai will hold a grand welcome at that time. After staying in Shanghai for four days, it will sail south.

Large Fire in Zhabei During the Day

Datong Road, Hengtong Road

Millions Worth of Houses Lost

At 12:40 yesterday, a fire broke out at 553 Datong Road, Zhabei, south of the railway (in the tin-roofed house facing west, belonging to Fu Shirong, a Ningbo native who runs the Chuan Baoxing bamboo shop), because of carelessly drying a quilt on the stove. The houses where Fu lived were close to the railway. At that time, the northwest wind was very strong, so the flames spread to the southeast. After the Taiyangmiao Police Station of the Xinzha Branch learned of this, it immediately called the Fire Brigade and sent a belt car to extinguish the fire. However, the wind was very strong, and in less than two hours, the fire spread to the tin-roofed and tiled bungalows on the left, right, and behind, totaling 16 shops from 527 to 559, including Liu Rongsen, Tan Xinchang, Quan Zhentai, Tan Yuchang, Yuanshengchang, Jiang Yixing, Liu Yongcheng, Sanhecheng, Yan Yongxing, Ge Shunxing, Jishengyuan, etc., new and old furniture shops. Most of the warehouses behind them were destroyed. After the investigation by Zhu Liming, Yang Jintang, and other police station chiefs, it was found that a total of 45 tin-roofed houses were destroyed, each worth 50 yuan, totaling 2,250 yuan, and 23 tiled bungalows, each worth about 200 yuan, totaling 4,600 yuan. The business assets were worth about 4,300 yuan, totaling more than 11,000 yuan in losses. The arsonist, Fu Shirong, was arrested and sent to the Xinzha Branch, which reported it to the Inspection Office of the Public Security Bureau. At 2:10, a fire alarm was reported at 36 Hengtong Road, the Wanxing cigarette and wine shop opened by Wu Junliang. Smoke filled the air, and the roof was pierced in a moment. Although fire trucks from various sections came to rescue, the fire was extinguished after 4:00. After investigation, it was learned that a total of five buildings at 36, 38, 40, 42, and 44 Hengtong Road were destroyed, with an estimated loss of more than 4,000 yuan. The arsonist, Wu Junliang, 34 years old, from Jiading, was arrested. According to Shen Taiyuan, who runs a tofu shop, a piece of oilcloth was placed on Wu Junliang's signboard, causing the fire. According to Xu Buchi and other neighbors, Wu has fire insurance of 1,500 yuan with the New World Company. Director Gong of the branch bureau is investigating the matter to find out if there are any other circumstances.

China Industrial Bank Audit Results

The Commercial Sector Still Has a Surplus

Head Office Accounts Sealed

The China Industrial Bank went bankrupt. Manager Qin Baoyuan absconded with funds in advance. Lu Xihou, the executive director of the Qunyi Syndicate bearing the economic responsibility for the bank, and the new manager Lu Mengxiang, etc., were prosecuted by the police. Because Lu Xihou had co-founded the International Jockey Club with a certain Westerner in the summer, spending a large sum of money, but the authorities did not approve the registration, causing the club to disappear without a trace. The funds spent on purchasing horses and hiring jockeys, etc., were supposedly advanced by the bank. A request was made to send personnel to audit the accounts. The First Special District Local Court appointed two accountants, Xu Yongzuo, etc., to audit all the accounts. The day before yesterday, after the court examined the proposals of Lu et al., it ruled that the criminal part of the case be adjourned for further hearing. Thereupon, civil judges, responding to the request for liquidation from Lu et al., investigated Lu Xihou and Lu Mengxiang, ordering them to immediately provide a list of assets and debts, so that personnel could be dispatched to handle the liquidation. This has been detailed in our newspaper. It is now known that all new and old account books of the bank and the head office were, according to accountant Xu, sealed by the police when he was instructed to audit the accounts, so he could only audit those that had not been seized. The audit results showed that the commercial sector of the bank owed 449,303.34 yuan, while 563,862.60 yuan was owed to the bank. The two offset each other, leaving a surplus. However, the savings sector owed 498,151.75 yuan, while 74,640.47 yuan was owed to the sector. The two offset each other with a significant deficit. When the commercial and savings sectors were combined, the statistical difference was more than 300,850 yuan. According to the accountant's report, 233,965.73 yuan of this difference was owed by the head office. Because the accounts of the head office were still sealed, there was no way to investigate, and the nature and use of the shortage were unknown. In addition, 74,986.29 yuan was used for renting land and building houses at the Nanjing Road branch, and for purchasing equipment for the Foch Road branch on the Tianzhu Church Street in the South City, as well as for the start-up costs of various branches, stamp paper fees, etc. Although the International Jockey Club had a current account, the audit report did not mention it, as Lu Xihou stated, the funds had been cleared. Now, in order to thoroughly understand the bank's accounts, the court intends to issue a warrant, ordering the police to send all the seized account books of the head office to the court, so that the appointed liquidator can conduct a detailed review. The truth will surely come to light in the near future.

Crackdown on Unlicensed Charter Cars

Nearly Two Hundred People Fined

Each Fined One Yuan

The Public Concession Bureau's Vehicle Department has observed that the number of unlicensed charter cars on various streets has been increasing daily. The drivers of these cars spend the entire day with a car in hand, soliciting passengers arbitrarily on the roads, which is even more detestable than ordinary rickshaws. This seriously obstructs traffic and affects road administration. Therefore, a crackdown method has been planned. All legitimate charter cars that are not unlicensed must submit a receipt when applying for a license fee. When the owner is out with a car, he should hand over this arm badge to the driver to wear on his arm. Unlicensed charter cars will not be given arm badges for identification. This will be implemented on the first of this month. The police authorities have issued a notice to all Chinese and foreign detectives in all police stations to pay attention during their duties. If a driver pulling a charter car is found without an arm badge,

He will be immediately detained. As a result, it has become difficult for general unlicensed charter car drivers to pass off as licensed. In recent days, those who have been detained and punished are already numerous. The number of detentions by each police station the day before yesterday was particularly high. Among them, the Old Gate and Central Police Stations, due to the diligent inspection by Chinese Deputy Head Lu Dagong and others, achieved good results. After these drivers were detained at the police station, each was required to deposit one yuan in cash as bail for release. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special District Local Court for trial. After questioning by the criminal court judge, each was fined one yuan. After this strict crackdown, unlicensed charter cars may disappear from the streets.

A Scrubbing Brush Claims a Life

Mother Suspects Daughter of Hiding It on Purpose

Daughter Commits Suicide in Resentment

Gong Shen, a woman from Haimen, 22 years old, her husband Gong Aqing, a cotton merchant, and her mother Shen Shi, etc., lived together at No. 13 Rongli, Tianbao Road, Zhabei. The family was usually harmonious. But the day before yesterday, Shen Shi intended to wash clothes and had placed a scrubbing brush. At this moment, she suddenly could not find it anywhere and suspected that her daughter had deliberately hidden it. She immediately began to scold her. Although her niece tried to defend her, she was ultimately not understood by her mother. Therefore, she alone went to the bedroom and hanged herself when no one was around. By the time her mother discovered it, it was too late for regret. She immediately called her son-in-law to help her take her down, but she was already barely breathing. She was sent to Guangren Hospital for treatment, but to no avail, and she soon died. The hospital reported to the Xinza Police Station, which ordered detectives to investigate. The body was then transported to the Feren Road Morgue for autopsy. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Local Court appointed Prosecutor Tang, along with two forensic doctors, Wei and Zhang, and clerk Wang Zuyi, etc., to come to the morgue to examine the body. After identifying the body, and after hearing the previous account from the deceased's husband, Gong Aqing, Prosecutor Tang ruled that the deceased, Gong Shen, female, had indeed died by hanging herself before death. The body was handed over to her husband, Gong Aqing, for coffining and burial with a signed statement.

Wu Peizhen Requests a Divorce from Her Deaf-Mute Husband

| Rescheduled for Further Hearing at 2 PM on the 15th

Chen Wu Peizhen, a local young woman, sued her husband Chen Senlin (who is deaf and mute) in the Local Court through lawyer Yang Changchi for severe injury from poisoning and abandonment, requesting a divorce, compensation for damages, and the return of dowry ornaments. The grounds for the divorce were that her husband's temperament was fierce, he often beat her, and he had affairs. He would only return late at night. On the morning of August 30 this year, she attempted suicide by jumping into the river, but was rescued. She has been hospitalized in Nanyang Hospital for many days, but no one from her husband's family has visited her, which is truly a sign of broken affection, etc. The defendant, Chen Senlin, hired lawyer Lu Qi to defend him and filed a counterclaim, requesting that the plaintiff's lawsuit be dismissed. It was found that the plaintiff was born out of wedlock. Her own father and legal mother used to run a lime business in Shanghai, but have returned to their hometown for many years. At the time of the engagement, the matchmaker stated that because the other party (mother and daughter) did not want to live in the countryside and were helpless in Shanghai, they only needed to be provided with food and clothing and did not seek a high match.

Aid Patriotic Martyrs Association Sends Representatives to Petition in Beijing

Requesting Amnesty for Liu Chongwu, etc., to Console Public Sentiment

The Shanghai Aid Patriotic Martyrs Association, considering that the Fifth Plenary Session will open on the tenth of this month, and in order to petition the session to request an explicit amnesty for patriotic martyrs Liu Chongwu, Cao Songshou, Tian Yongyang, etc., has appointed representatives Hu Fengxiang, Chen Jiufeng, Yu Yaoqiu, Chen Peide, Wang Jingdong, etc., five people in total, who will take the night express train to Beijing tonight to petition the session, the Central Political Council, the Ministry of Judicial Administration, etc., requesting that amnesty be granted to console public sentiment. The details are recorded separately below.

Petitioning in Beijing Tonight

The Aid Patriotic Martyrs Association believes that patriotic martyrs Liu Chongwu, etc., committed offenses in the 21st year of the Republic out of indignation at the shamelessness of treacherous merchants. A moment of passionate impulse led them to issue warnings, resulting in their being caught in the legal net. Although various legal groups in this city have repeatedly petitioned the authorities requesting amnesty, it has not been granted. Unfortunately, Pan Hongsheng died due to excessive punishment, and the martyrs in prison have no release date. As things stand, their grievances cannot be redressed. Now that the Fifth Plenary Session will open on December 10th, in order to request the session to explicitly grant amnesty, a general meeting of representatives from various organizations was convened on November 18th. Hu Fengxiang, Chen Jiufeng, Yu Yaoqiu, Chen Peide, Wang Jingdong, etc., five people were appointed as representatives to take the petition to Beijing and separately petition the Fifth Plenary Session, the National Government, the Central Political Council, the Judicial Yuan, and the Ministry of Judicial Administration, etc. It is now known that the representatives, due to the proximity of the session, have specifically decided to take the night express train to Beijing tonight to petition, and will also contact various legal groups in Beijing to jointly appeal to the authorities, striving to achieve their goal.

Request for Amnesty

Request regarding patriotic martyrs Liu Chongwu, Tian Shuiyang, Cao Songshou, whose cases have been sent back by the Supreme Court for retrial but have still been sentenced to heavy penalties, requesting approval of amnesty to uphold the national spirit and console the people. In the winter of the 21st year of the Republic, patriotic martyrs Liu Chongwu, Pan Hongsheng, Tian Shuiyang, Cao Songshou, etc., were indignant at the enemy's merchants engaging in communication with the enemy, the dumping of enemy goods, the decline of national goods, and the despair of the people's livelihood. Rather than sit and wait for death, they rose up to seek survival. Therefore, they disregarded everything and used various methods to issue stern warnings to treacherous merchants. Their motives were entirely out of patriotism. The martyrs deeply felt that the quantity of enemy goods flooding the market was directly proportional to the strength of the enemy and inversely proportional to the strength of our country. The flood of enemy goods and the surge in import surplus caused outrage to anyone with a conscience. However, since diplomatic relations had not been severed, there was no way to impose legal sanctions on the treacherous merchants who pursued profit, and warning behavior could not avoid being restricted by legal provisions. (Omitted section)... It is found that if this case is observed solely from the surface of the actions, it is indeed not permitted by law. However, the victimized treacherous merchants and the defendants had no prior acquaintance and no grievances. The warning action also did not provide any benefit for the defendants. It was only because the treacherous merchants traded in enemy goods, harming the interests of the entire country and the entire nation, and the national law did not punish such evil people, that the defendants stepped forward to engage in a private fight with treacherous national traitors. Their purpose was to uphold the interests of the country and the nation, with absolutely no other. Now, people who uphold the interests of the country and the nation have been imprisoned for a long time, while treacherous merchants who engage in private interests and harm the country are protected by law. How can this comfort the national spirit and promote justice? The city's Bar Association, seeing this, suggested to the Ministry of Judicial Administration in the winter of the 21st year of the Republic that a separate jury court be set up to hear cases where the motive was patriotism but the law was violated. Although it was approved, it was not implemented. Recently, Pan Hongsheng died in prison from illness caused by grief and resentment. The remaining Liu Chongwu, Tian Shuiyang, Cao Songshou, etc., are also facing the danger of following in Pan Hongsheng's footsteps. The representatives of various organizations present, after consultation and unanimous agreement, specially appointed representatives to jointly implore approval of amnesty. The country is fortunate, and the nation is fortunate. Respectfully presented, (omitted below).

A strip of armband will be issued along with the license, and the car owner is ordered to hand this armband to the driver to wind around his arm when taking the car out. Unlicensed charter cars will not be given armbands for identification. This will be implemented on the first of this month. The police authorities have issued a notice to all Chinese and foreign detectives in all police stations to pay attention during their duties. If a driver pulling a charter car is found without an armband,

He will be immediately detained. As a result, it has become difficult for general unlicensed charter car drivers to pass off as licensed. Murdered Male Corpse Found on Desolate Land on Fulu Road

Looks like a Villager, Murdered and Then Body Moved to the Spot

A Card with Shi Zhaolan's Name Was Found in His Pocket

West Police Officer No. 209 and West Police Officer No. 106 of the French Concession Foch Police Station, while patrolling Fulu Road at 7:00 AM yesterday morning, discovered an unidentified male corpse that had been hacked to death on the desolate land behind No. 18 Fude Lane. He was approximately 30 years old, with his head facing northeast and his feet facing southwest, lying supine on the ground. He was wearing a melon-skin cap, a black cloth cotton robe, black cloth-lined trousers, black foreign socks, and black cloth-faced cloth-bottomed Duzuo shoes. His clothes were already worn and old, resembling a villager from Jiangbei. His left neck appeared to have been chopped with an axe, with a wound approximately half an inch deep. There were two small knife holes in the back of his head. The West Police Officers immediately reported to the police station, and Chinese and foreign detectives went to investigate. A card was found in his pocket, with only the three characters "Shi Zhaolan" and nothing else. Judging by the situation, it appeared that he had been murdered and then abandoned here. The body was immediately transported by car to the Tongren Fuyuan branch hall for autopsy. A report was sent to the Second Special Court, which appointed Prosecutor Wang Ren, along with a forensic doctor, a clerk, etc., to come to the morgue at noon to examine the body. As no family members of the deceased were found, the official instructed that the body be handed over to Tongren Fuyuan Hall for photographing and burial, pending identification by family members. The French Concession Police Department was also instructed to notify all detectives on duty to investigate and arrest the murderer for interrogation.

Family Dispute Over the Estate of the Deceased Owner of Ren Changtai Candle Shop

Friends' Mediation Falls Short

Ren Changtai Incense and Candle Shop, next to Hongmiao on Nanjing Road, was opened by Huang Xunhua, a native of Zhenhai, Ningbo. In addition to the Hongmiao shop, Huang also had Ren Changtai branches on Chongqing Road and at the Eight Immortals Bridge in the French Concession. His legal wife, Huang Hua Caiqin, and their son, Huang Yongchuan, lived in the Chongqing Road branch, while his concubine, Chu Yuzhuo, and his adopted daughter, Huang Hanqing, lived in the Eight Immortals Bridge branch. This state of affairs had been going on for years. Because the business of both the main and branch stores was good, yielding substantial profits annually, the family lived comfortably and could usually get along peacefully. In September of this year, Huang Xunyao died of illness, leading to a dispute between the wife and concubine over the division of the estate. Friends such as Bai Liewu had made every effort to mediate and proposed a settlement. The attitude of both parties had shown signs of softening. Those acting as Lu Zhonglian were happy that the dispute could be resolved. Unexpectedly, the effort fell short because the issue of Chu Yuzhuo's status was once again fiercely debated. Chu, in her capacity as the legal guardian of her daughter Hanqing, hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Huang Hua Caiqin and her fourteen-year-old son Huang Yongchuan in the First Special District Local Court for the division of the estate. She claimed that when Huang Xunhua married her, he said he had no wife. Only after they were married did she learn that Xunhua had a wife. She argued with him, and Xunhua agreed to treat her as "both heads of the family". Now that her husband had passed away, all the property was in the hands of the defendant. She requested that the court order the defendant to hand over her share, which amounted to more than 38,000 yuan. The court summoned them previously, but the case was postponed due to the defendant's absence. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Qiao held a court session. The defendant also hired lawyer Li Cishan to appear in court. In addition to responding to the plaintiff's lawsuit, Xu also filed a counterclaim, requesting an order for Chu to hand over the Eight Immortals Bridge branch to Huang Hua Caiqin for management. He also stated that this case could have been resolved peacefully and requested that the plaintiff be persuaded to settle. Judge Qiao granted a three-week postponement, directing both parties to conduct settlement negotiations outside the court. If no settlement was reached by the deadline, they would be summoned again.

Cold Weather Prompts Social Affairs Bureau to Help the Poor

Shelters Set Up in the South of Shanghai

Soup Kitchens Planned in Zhabei

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, recognizing that the cold weather has caused hardship for the general poor, who have nowhere to seek shelter, has selected the Huzhou Guild Hall in the south of Shanghai and the Chao-Hui Villa on Xietu Road to set up shelters. In Zhabei, charitable organizations will set up soup kitchens. The details are recorded below:

Shelters: According to officials of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, the bureau, together with the Shanghai Charity Organizations Joint Association, has set up the first shelter in the Chaozhou Guild Hall. The shelter began accepting the poor on the first of this month. As of today, the number of people sheltered has reached more than 500. The second shelter has been selected at the Chao-Hui Villa on Xietu Road. The buildings there are spacious, enough to accommodate two to three thousand people. However, because the Security Department's communications team was originally stationed there, the Social Affairs Bureau consulted with Director Yang and requested that they relocate. Director Yang agreed to relocate as soon as a suitable building was found. As soon as the communications team moves out, acceptance can begin. The expenses of both shelters, in addition to being planned by charitable organizations, have also been approved by the municipal government for an allocation of 3,000 yuan to provide assistance.

Overseas Chinese Merchants in Singapore Plan to Open a National Products Exhibition

Chamber of Commerce Representative Huang Manshi Returns Home to Negotiate

Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday, Talked About How Overseas Chinese Welcome National Products

Huang Manshi, the representative of the Singapore Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, returned to China to investigate national products and negotiate the opening of a national products exhibition. He arrived in Shanghai from Tianjin and Beijing yesterday. A reporter from Xin Sheng News Agency visited him at his lodging and received a detailed account. The details are recorded below:

Preparing to Open an Exhibition: The total population of Singapore is more than 440,000, of which Chinese people account for approximately 330,000, accounting for three-quarters. Businesses there are mostly operated by Chinese, and the consumption of goods is also mostly by Chinese. Although overseas Chinese live in foreign countries, their love for their country is very ardent. During the September 18th and January 28th incidents, the donations from overseas Chinese there were very large. They are particularly eager to use national products. However, due to the lack of national products in the area, they cannot purchase them. The Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, deeply aware of this, is preparing to hold a national products exhibition there and promote the sale of national products.

Returning Home to Negotiate the Collection of Goods: Huang was specially dispatched on the 6th of last month to return to China with the tasks of (1) investigating national products in our country, (2) negotiating the opening of an exhibition, with the aim of promoting the sale of national products. After arriving in Shanghai, he will go to Beijing to report to Minister of Industry Chen Gongbo and negotiate the opening of a national products exhibition. Minister Chen was very supportive and willing to assist. He will also go to Tianjin and Beijing to solicit national products from various national products organizations to be transported to Singapore to participate in the exhibition. The results were very satisfactory. After returning to Shanghai, he will visit the Chinese Industrial Federation, the National Chamber of Commerce Federation, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the National Products Production and Sales Cooperation Association, and other organizations to negotiate.

Exhibition Focuses on Promotion: Various national products organizations are preparing

To participate in the Manila Exhibition of the Carnival, and have decided to take this opportunity to divide the national products for participation into two parts: one part to participate in the Carnival, and one part to participate in the Singapore Exhibition. The date for the opening of the National Products Exhibition will be decided after the Carnival closes. It is called an exhibition, but it is actually a promotion. At that time, the organizations formed by various national products industrial and commercial firms participating will send representatives to go, and the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce will send staff to assist in the exhibition and promotion. The expenses can also be saved, and language barriers can be avoided, as the local dialects are mainly from Fujian and Guangdong provinces.

Foreign Goods Compete with the Exhibition: The British, in view of the dumping of Japanese goods,

Held British goods exhibitions in Singapore twice last year and this year. Last year, 75 industrial and commercial firms participated, and this year, 144 industrial and commercial firms participated. It is planned to hold it once a year, and next year it will be expanded to 300 industrial and commercial firms. Overseas Chinese there hope that our country's national products exhibition will be held. Also, this year an American merchant brought Chinese goods to Singapore for exhibition, which was suspected by overseas Chinese. Why should national products be promoted by foreigners instead of finding ways themselves to benefit foreigners?

Overseas Chinese Eagerly Hope for Realization: Now, overseas Chinese all hope that the national

Products exhibition will be realized soon, bringing glory to our country's national products and giving overseas Chinese a good impression. Therefore, Huang's return to Shanghai this time will include visiting various emerging industrial factories in the country and investigating our country's national products in order to promote them upon his return. After the negotiations are completed, he will return to Singapore from Shanghai and make preparations for holding it on a fixed date.

Soup Kitchens: As for Zhabei, charitable organizations have decided

To set up a soup kitchen at the original site of the Second Soup Kitchen on Liuying Road to provide porridge. However, the issue of funding has not been adequately resolved. Therefore, the charitable organizations will convene a board meeting within a few days to discuss raising funds. Once the funds have been discussed and decided, the soup kitchen will be set up immediately to help the poor.

City Chamber of Commerce Publishes "The National Goods Bridge" and "Trademark Compilation"

Two Monumental Works on National Goods Factories

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce has always paid close attention to matters such as investigating, introducing, and promoting national goods. In recent years, it has received numerous requests daily from overseas Chinese chambers of commerce and chambers of commerce in various provinces and cities to inquire about the names and trademarks of national goods manufacturers. Therefore, it was decided that the Chamber's Commodity Exhibition Hall would compile a book called "The National Goods Bridge" for reference. At the same time, regarding trademarks, in addition to the previously sold "Japanese Trademark Compilation," a "East Asian Trademark Compilation" has recently been released, bringing together a comprehensive collection of Japanese and Chinese commodity trademarks. The above two books are valuable publications for the national goods industry and the business community. The contents of the two books are described below:

Newly Compiled "The National Goods Bridge"

The first edition of "The National Goods Bridge" was published in 1925, and a revised edition was published in 1930. The materials used at that time included five items: product name, trademark, factory name, place of manufacture, and issuing organization, categorized for easy reference. Readers often referred to it as a national goods directory. Now, because the Chinese people's perception of national goods is more profound than before, starting with this edition, in addition to the original items, all information about the factory is added, such as capital, establishment date, manager's name, telegraph, and telephone numbers. The content is divided into seventeen categories: (1) Textile and Dyeing, (2) Clothing and Ornaments, (3) Food and Beverages, (4) Household Goods, (5) Travel Goods, (6) Miscellaneous Daily Necessities, (7) Construction, (8) Education, (9) Toys, (10) Hygiene, (11) Cosmetics, (12) Rubber Products, (13) Industrial Raw Materials, (14) Electrical Machinery and Appliances, (15) Machinery, (16) Miscellaneous Handicrafts, and (17) Tobacco and Alcohol. It includes the products of more than 2,000 national goods factories, first listing Shanghai and then other ports. The national goods listed are limited to those that meet the national goods standards announced by the Ministry of Industry in 1932. The book is printed in fine Tianzhang Daolin paper in a thick volume, priced at five real silver jiao per copy. Any formal national goods organizations and institutions with official letters can obtain a copy from the Chamber's Commodity Exhibition Hall by enclosing five fen for postage.

"East Asian Trademark Compilation"

This book collects all registered and approved Chinese and Japanese trademarks from the establishment of the Trademark Bureau in 1912 up to December 31, 1932, including those registered and approved by the former National Registration Bureau and the Trademark Bureau, as well as those registered and approved by the former Beijing Trademark Bureau. It includes 70 categories for China, with 1,672 pages, and 67 categories for Japan, with 856 pages, totaling more than 3,500 pages and containing over 10,000 kinds of goods. It brings together a comprehensive collection of Japanese and Chinese trademarks, comparing them by category for easy inspection. It also includes the new and old trademark laws, implementing regulations, registration instructions, and application forms, making it a valuable reference for lawyers, accountants, and the industrial sector. The entire book is finely printed by the Zhonghua Book Company in a thick volume with Western binding, priced at fifteen silver dollars. It is sold by the general and branch stores of the Zhonghua Book Company in various provinces and cities, the dispatch office of the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce, and the publishing department of the Xinsheng News Agency at No. 9 Chongde Lane, Simalu, Shanghai.

The Yellow Society to Hold Exhibition

The Southeast Touring Exhibition organized by the Zhejiang Construction Department pays great attention to the construction, scenery, and places of interest in the five provinces. It invited celebrities from the literary and art circles to visit and publicize them this spring. Huangshan Mountain, a famous historical site, has been a place for general men of letters to admire, chant, copy, and paint since its development in the Tang Dynasty. Painters such as Mei Qushan, Shi Hongren, and Shi Tao have all gained great fame for writing about Huangshan scenery. The wonder of the scenery is like a fairyland. In May of this year, Ye Xianyu, Zhong Shan Yin, Ma Guoliang, Lang Jingshan, Chen Jiazhen, Chen Wanli, Xu Tianzhang, Luo Gusun, and Shao Yuxiang, photographers from major newspapers and magazines in Shanghai, were invited by the Zhejiang Construction Department to visit Huangshan. Ye and others then initiated the Yellow Society to promote art and publicize Huangshan's scenic spots. At this time, films and paintings were taken, totaling more than a thousand pieces. In order to share this with the people of Shanghai, a selection of several hundred pieces will be exhibited at the address of the YMCA in Baxianqiao for three days starting from the 15th of this month. Tickets will be sold for one jiao each, and all proceeds will be donated to the YMCA's Christmas children's party gifts.

Xie Fuchu Organizes Overseas Chinese Industry Investigation Delegation

Overseas Chinese Xie Fuchu previously summoned wealthy overseas Chinese merchants from the Dutch East Indies to return to China to organize an industry investigation delegation to conduct on-site investigations in the northwest, southwest, and inland provinces, in order to invest in various undertakings. The organization had been completed, and it was originally scheduled to gather in Shanghai and prepare to depart. However, he was hospitalized due to illness, and the delegation's work was suspended. Xie was ill for two months and has just been discharged from the hospital. According to him, "I am familiar with many overseas Chinese at home and abroad. The motive for organizing this overseas Chinese industry investigation delegation is that, after the loss of the Northeast, there is no way to survive without developing the Northwest. People with insight share this view, and overseas Chinese also have a strong patriotic enthusiasm. In recent years, they have been oppressed by the governments of their places of residence and are also very willing to return to China to invest and develop industries. Therefore, everyone agreed after consultation. Moreover, this delegation has already been organized and cannot be disbanded due to my illness. Although a small number of overseas Chinese are hesitant due to fear of the cold weather in the interior, I will strongly persuade them and actively proceed to ensure that we depart as soon as possible."

The Nanjing Road Businessmen's Association in this city has recently been paying attention to disaster relief in various provinces, and various charitable organizations have also been raising funds for emergency relief. The association's area is located in the commercial center of Shanghai. Even though the market is depressed, it is obligatory to donate to disaster relief. Shanghai Bank Robbery Case Transferred

On the morning of the 21st of last month, at around 9:00 AM, the Shanghai Bank sent personnel to deliver 5,200 yuan to the savings office of Jiaotong University on Haig Road in the French Concession. It was robbed on the way. Chen Goudi, Zhang Zilong, and eight other criminals were arrested by the Yulin Road Police Station and sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation. This has already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, the police sent Chen and the other criminals to the Third Criminal Court. Li Zhishan, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, stated that this case should be transferred to the Second Special Court for trial. However, defendant Zhang Ganlong, at 3:30 AM on October 27, gathered three accomplices and robbed the home of Gong Guochen, a local resident at No. 1846 Xinzha Road, of property worth 416 yuan. The victim identified the defendant at the police station as being present at the robbery. Please handle this case strictly. Gong Guochen and his wife, Xu, testified that the defendant was holding a pistol at the time. Zhang Zilong's confession was evasive. Judge Bi Xiaofen sentenced Zhang Zilong to seven years in prison. The number of days of detention before the final judgment was commuted to one day of imprisonment for every two days. The French police sent a letter from Chinese detective Yang Yilong, requesting a transfer. The court asked each defendant about their age and place of origin. After a brief review, the court ordered that Chen Goudi, Tan Jinbiao, Yao Sheng, Huang Shun, Zhang Zilong, Zhou, A Mei, and Zhu Xuelong be transferred to the Second Special District of Shanghai for trial.

Germany's Greatest War Film

"Storm Troopers" to be Screened in Shanghai

With Chinese Subtitles

"Storm Troopers" is a major German war film. The film is purely a performance of the truth of war, does not tell a story, and is all about the terrible situation of the front lines and trenches. The realism of the filming is shocking. During the filming of this film, a total of 30,000 pounds of gunpowder and eight tons of explosives were used. The amount is enough to turn the entire city of Shanghai into powder. The actors in the film are all soldiers who personally participated in the war, specially hired by the film company's manager. Therefore, the various sections performed are incomparable to general actors in love films. There are explosions of large grenade launchers, continuous artillery fire, fireballs all over the ground, as bright as electricity, and all destruction is clearly revealed. When shells enter the ground, they immediately form huge holes. Soldiers hiding in trenches are immediately destroyed and fly into the air. The most essential part is when the enemy's tanks drive into the German lines and use their huge power to wreak all kinds of destruction. Behind the tanks, enemy soldiers swarm forward, and machine guns fire, as dense as firecrackers, with the dead lying everywhere. Finally, the tanks are destroyed by artillery fire. The tension of the plot is something we have not yet witnessed. In addition, the film company has spared no expense to include Chinese subtitles in the film, which is also unprecedented for foreign films. There is very little dialogue in the film. Everything is clear on the screen. The film will be named "Storm Troopers" and will be screened in Shanghai soon. It is expected that its success will not be less than when it was shown in Europe.

Great Sales of Red-Label Special-Price Goods at the Daxin National Silk and Satin Bureau

The Daxin National Silk and Satin Bureau on Simmalu and Shilou has been holding a winter sale since yesterday. In addition to selling various exquisite domestic products at a 10% discount, it is also selling ten kinds of special-price goods at low prices marked with red labels. People from all walks of life consider the bureau to be a general organization that completely promotes domestic products and has no concerns about passing off foreign goods as domestic goods. In order to clarify the competitive reality of improved domestic silk and satin, domestic silk factories have rushed to display their latest products, so that those who love domestic silk and satin can have the opportunity to see them first. Yesterday was the first day of the bureau's winter sale, and business was extremely crowded. Sales of red-label special-price goods were particularly smooth. Because the bureau complied with the association's decision and did not mark the actual price of the discounted goods in the advertisement, the price was indeed unexpectedly low. It is estimated that yesterday's sales were strongest for electric crepe, fragrant crepe, colored wool gabardine, and various soft satins.

Yaopuer New Leap Electric Stove

The various electric light bulbs and electric fans produced by the China Yaopuer Electric Appliance Factory are of high quality, solid materials, power-saving, and durable, and have long been popular. It is heard that the factory has newly produced a kind of electric stove, with a novel form, which has never been seen in China. Its heat can spread around, the power is about 2,700 watts. Because the manufacturing method is particularly fine, it consumes very little power. If one is placed in a room, the joy of gathering around the stove for warmth will be harmonious. It is expected that this product will go without saying once it is released.

The Legislative Yuan Publishes a Compilation of Constitutions of Various Countries

Since the Legislative Yuan began accepting pre-orders for the Compilation of Constitutions of Various Countries last month, libraries, schools, and institutions at home and abroad have been very enthusiastic in ordering it. It is heard that both the upper and lower volumes have been published. The content includes the constitutions and provisional laws of our country in the past, as well as the current constitutions of more than seventy large and small countries in the world. It also includes the draft constitution of the Republic of China that the Legislative Yuan is currently drafting. Each collection is compiled with detailed indexes. If you want to know how a country's constitution stipulates a certain issue, you can find it with a quick search. The entire book is two huge volumes, priced at twelve yuan, special price nine yuan six jiao. It is distributed by the Hanwen Zhengkai Printing Company on Shandong Road in this city.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the weather around Shandong is clear and cold, with varying light northerly to northeasterly winds. The middle reaches of the Yangtze River are cloudy and cold, with fog in the morning and variable winds. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River have strong, cool winds from the northwest to the north. The East China Sea and the Taiwan Strait are overcast, with strong seasonal winds. The weather between the Ryukyu Islands and the Ogasawara Islands is bad due to a northward-moving hurricane. The center of the hurricane was within 120 miles of 24 degrees north latitude and 140 degrees east longitude at 2:00 PM, moving north. The wind force is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the highest temperature in this city was 50.7 degrees and the lowest was 35.8 degrees. On the same day last year, the highest was 60.4 degrees and the lowest was 42.8 degrees.

The Huachun Weaving Factory's Retail Department Opens Tomorrow

The Huachun Weaving Factory was founded in 1917. It built a factory building in Zhabei Zhonghua Xinlu, covering an area of 20 mu. It weaves more than 100 kinds of Pagoda brand pure silk socks, underwear, etc., which are sold all over the country. For nearly 20 years, it has been quite reputable. Recently, it established a distribution office in Nanjiulu Zhejianglu East to directly supply the needs of people from all walks of life. The second floor has a national goods service department, joining more than 40 famous factories. It will officially open tomorrow, with many special sacrifices prepared.

Educational News

National Vocational Education Conference Opens

First General Assembly Held at 9:00 AM

More Than Fifty Representatives and Forty Proposals Arrive

The National Vocational Education Conference convened by the Ministry of Education opened at the Ministry of Education today (the 7th). Except for Yunnan, which replied by telegram that it was unable to send representatives to participate due to time constraints, representatives from Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Fujian, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Guangdong, Guangxi, Shandong, Henan, Chahar, Hebei, Gansu, Suiyuan, Qinghai, Guizhou, Shaanxi, Sichuan, Shanxi, Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, Rehe, Beijing, Shanghai, Ping, Qingdao, Guangzhou, and 30 other provinces and cities, as well as the Weihaiwei Management Office, a total of 31 places with more than 50 people, plus members hired by the Ministry of Education and representatives from various institutions and Ministry of Education personnel, totaled more than 60 participants. The list of participants and the outline of the proposals are recorded below.

General Assembly This Morning

(Nanjing, 6th Dispatch) The 56 representatives from various provinces and cities, including Xiang Shaoxuan, who attended the National Vocational Education Discussion Conference, reported to the ministry successively on the 6th. At 9:00 AM on the 7th, the first general assembly will be held in the auditorium of the Ministry of Education. Minister of Education Wang Shijie will preside over the meeting and report on the significance of convening the vocational education discussion conference. Next, representatives from various provinces and cities will report on the general situation of vocational education in their respective provinces and cities. After that, the list of group committee members will be determined. Lunch will be held at the ministry at noon. In the afternoon, group meetings will be held to review the proposals in groups first, and then submit them to the general assembly for discussion on the 9th. It is heard that up to the 6th, a total of 40 proposals have been received from various small cities. The Labor Exhibition Association presented each representative to the Vocational Education Discussion Conference with a badge, so that they could attend the conference at any time and visit.
