The Vice Minister also attended the meeting and delivered a speech.

Snippets of Proposals

Proposals from the Ministry of Education: The following is a general outline of the proposals submitted by the Ministry of Education for the National Vocational Education Discussion Conference:

Group 1 (Regarding administrative personnel, funding, laws, and organization)

(1) Regarding the proposal to establish full-time personnel in the education bureaus of each province and city to handle and inspect vocational schools:

(1) Within the educational science department in charge of schools, there must be at least one qualified full-time staff member to handle vocational education and vocational guidance.

(2) Among the supervisors or instructors, one to two must be designated to supervise vocational schools at all levels on a full-time basis.

(2) Regarding the proposal of how each small city should realize the standards for establishing and allocating funds for secondary schools set by the Ministry:

(1) For provinces and cities that already have planned to realize the standards set by the Ministry in stages and years, how to effectively comply within the limits set by the Ministry.

(2) For provinces and cities that do not yet have planned to realize the standards set by the Ministry, how to quickly formulate and submit them to the Ministry for approval and implementation.

(3) How should the increased funding for vocational schools in each province and city be used to strengthen existing vocational school equipment, followed by the establishment of vocational schools? (3) Regarding the proposal of how to supervise the implementation of laws and regulations on vocational education and what suggestions are there:

(1) How to supervise and implement the regulations on establishment of departments, funding, equipment, and practical training in vocational education laws and regulations.

(2) Should there be general methods for secondary schools with vocational departments and vocational schools with secondary school classes?

(3) How should the number of departments in each school be limited?

(4) Should the tuition fees for students in private vocational schools be appropriately modified? (4) Each province and city should, based on the industrial conditions of the province and city and the types of vocational talent needed, organize the existing vocational school departments and determine the types of departments to be established in the future.

(1) How should each province and city investigate the industrial conditions, vocational types, and talents needed in various fields of the province and city?

(2) Each province and city should conduct a detailed investigation of the departments established in existing public and private vocational schools to see if there are any biases or deficiencies, whether they meet the needs, and whether the graduates of each department are conveniently employed. If the established departments do not meet the needs, how to implement rational control and change to other departments?

(3) How should each public and private vocational school formulate concrete plans to add new departments in the future and implement them in stages and years?

(4) Each province and city should, within the possible scope, establish more vocational supplementary schools and junior vocational schools. The establishment of senior vocational schools should be based on the principle of one school for each type. The number of vocational schools related to business should be reduced as much as possible.

(5) Each province and city should quickly organize or strengthen existing vocational schools and ban poorly run public and private vocational schools.

(1) Each province and city should ensure that it effectively inspects the actual situation of public and private vocational schools throughout the province and city, assesses their performance, and reports to the Ministry for record.

(2) How should each province and city order the improvement or banning of poorly run public and private vocational schools with poor performance?

(6) Central and provincial/municipal subsidies for excellent public and private vocational schools

(1) How should each province and city annually formulate subsidy methods to allocate funds to subsidize the equipment or operating expenses of private vocational schools with excellent performance in the province or city, and how to reduce subsidies for private secondary schools. (2) Based on the results of inspections, the Ministry of Education should request the central government to allocate a certain amount of funds each year to subsidize part of the equipment or operating expenses of public and private vocational schools with excellent performance nationwide and formulate subsidy methods.

Group 2 (Regarding teacher training, promotion, guidance, and other matters)

(7) Training vocational school teachers:

(1) Each province and city needs teachers for vocational schools at all levels. How should they first determine the type of schools and departments based on the actual situation, and then investigate the types and quantities of teachers needed, and send a list to the Ministry?

(2) Senior vocational school teachers should be trained by the Ministry according to the types and quantities of teachers needed reported by each province and city, and designated to domestic schools above the corresponding specialty to train them. How to determine the quota for students sent by each province and city to study abroad?

(3) Junior vocational school teachers should be trained by each province by allocating special funds to designated vocational schools or schools above the specialty level with excellent performance.

(4) How to conduct vocational teacher registration and investigation of teachers who have received professional training for the purpose of introducing them?

(8) Promoting vocational supplementary education:

(1) How should the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce find ways to promote labor education laws and regulations, and order each province and city to order local industrial and commercial groups to establish vocational supplementary education institutions within a time limit so that apprentices in factories and shops can enter school for supplementary studies. (2) How should local education administrative agencies contact local industrial and commercial industries to set up various industry-related schools or supplementary schools within a time limit?

(3) How should local education administrative agencies contact local agricultural, industrial, and commercial circles to organize vocational supplementary education design committees?

(4) How should a certain amount be designated under the education funds of each province and city as the funds for promoting vocational supplementary education?

(9) Primary and secondary schools should strictly implement vocational guidance:

(1) How should the personnel in charge of vocational guidance in primary and secondary schools in each province and city supervise and order the principals of primary and secondary schools throughout the province and city to strictly implement vocational guidance within one academic year before graduation?

(2) How should education administrative agencies in each province and city hire experts to organize vocational guidance committees?

(3) How should education administrative agencies in each province and city hold vocational guidance holiday seminars regularly?

(4) How should each province and city conduct a survey of vocational conditions throughout the province and city and print and distribute vocational analysis booklets to each school?

(5) How should each province and city establish vocational guidance institutes and vocational referral agencies in the shortest possible time?

External proposals: In addition to the general outline of the conference proposals prepared by the Ministry of Education, several proposals have been sent from Hunan, Chahar, Suiyuan, and other provinces. The Chinese Vocational Education Society and others also have impromptu motions.

Detailed Record of the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Principals' Meeting

Director Zhou of the Department of Education Talks About the Current Situation of Education in Jiangsu Province

On the morning of the 5th, the 23rd Second Plenary Meeting of Jiangsu Provincial Secondary School Principals was held at Zhenjiang Normal School. In the afternoon, the principals attended a discussion meeting with Director Zhou Fohai of the Department of Education at the Department. In the evening at 6 o'clock, Zhou hosted a banquet for the principals at the Department. The general situation has been recorded in yesterday's newspaper. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Principals: Chen Shu (Suzhou Women's Normal School), Wu Xue (Wu Jie Normal School), Jiang Xuezhu (Songjiang Girls' Middle School), Yu Yu (Xuzhou Women's Normal School), An Shifeng (Yi Nong Agricultural School), Li Jianqing (Yunhe Township Normal School), Xu Jidun (Ruzhou Normal School), Cao Zhongquan (Donghai Normal School), Gu Kebin (Tai Cang Normal School), Zheng Pijiang (Women's Sericulture School), Peng Weiji (Changzhou Middle School), Xue Tianyou (Songjiang Vocational Middle School), Teng Shisong (Huangdu Township Normal School), Cao Chu (Suzhou Normal School), Zhang Jinan (Suqian Vocational School), Li Weizhang (Huaiyin Agricultural School), Tang Zhicai (Suzhou Agricultural School), Zhang Chuqing (Wusong Fisheries School), Wang Gang (Lianyungang Fisheries School), Sun Kui Jun (Zhang Bin acting for Nanjing Middle School), Sun Jiehuang (Wei Normal School), Sun Weizhan (Huaian Middle School), Zheng Xigu (Shangzhong School), Wu Hailou (Shihu Township Normal School), Wang Shipin (Tongzhou Middle School), Wu Wudi (Suzhou Middle School), Deng Bangdi (Suzhou Industrial School), Yan Yaofan (Xuzhou Middle School), Zhou Yigeng (Wuxi Normal School), Wu Dezhang (Yancheng Vocational School), Zhou Hushu (Yangzhou Middle School), Liu Hengjing (Nanjing Girls' Middle School), Jin Shuqiao (Wu Township Normal School), Zhang Cheng (Nanjing Middle School), Huang Zhitian (Qixia Township Normal School), Chairman Tang Zhicai, Recorder Cao Chu,

Matters for Discussion: 1. How should the Department's order to change the centralized military training makeup class method for the first grade be changed so that there is no difficulty? Resolution: State the following difficulties to the Department: (1) The second and third grades will be affected by the military training makeup class for graduation; (2) The female nurses have less training time and it is enough to cope with it. If they are concentrated with the boys, the girls' studies will inevitably be wasted; (3) The pre-determined makeup class method has been implemented in each school, and it is changed again at this time. There is a defense against the school's reputation, and the following suggestions are made: Please ask the General Inspectorate of Training to set the military training time for the first, second, and third grades of high school for 2 hours each, and hold a general exercise for one month in June of the last year. 2. The Department of Education issued a standard for inspecting the physical, chemical, and biological equipment of secondary schools. Should the association first collect statistics on the existing equipment of each school and submit them to the Department for reference in the allocation of temporary expenses in the 24th year? Resolution: Please pay attention to the balanced development of each school and make overall arrangements. 3. The training class for teachers should ask the association to submit a resolution to the Department of Education to stipulate the method. Resolution: Passed. 4. The province is currently handling land reports, and schools are no exception. In the future, schools will have to pay land price tax. Please ask the Department of Education to include the land price tax in the budget according to the size of the school area, or ask the Department of Finance to exempt the taxes payable by the provincial education agencies. Resolution: Please include it in the 24th year budget. 5. How to promote the graduates of agricultural schools? Resolution: Passed according to the original proposal. 6. How to decide the main points of the talk with the Director in the afternoon? Resolution: Please ask the Department to pay attention to the efficiency of personnel and seek the convenience of implementation separately.

Director Zhou's Speech: Director Zhou Fohai of the Jiangsu Department of Education talked about the convenience of inviting the principals of provincial middle schools to Zhenjiang for a meeting, inviting them to gather at the Department for communication, and at the same time listening to the actual management status of each school, or putting forward difficulties in school affairs for reference in improving secondary education in Jiangsu Province. After the reorganization of each school in Jiangsu Province, the principals and members of the Education Federation have been able to work hard on school affairs, so the academic style is simple and honest and full of vitality, and it can be gradually improved in the future. The education situation in each county is complicated and reorganization is not easy. The reasons are that the county magistrate does not pay attention to education, the selection of the director of the county education bureau is difficult, and the local concepts of the people in each county are too heavy, hindering the reorganization of county education, etc. At present, the Department is working hard to advocate the centralization and reorganization of school property in each county, so that the education funds of the county will gradually be enriched. The Department cherishes those who have outstanding abilities as directors of the education bureau and helps them to eliminate all obstacles so that they can stay in their positions for a long time. The infighting in education in each county of Jiangsu Province is the most serious. Now, except for Changshu, which is still in dispute, the rest of the counties can gradually get on the right track.

Salary Demand Trend of Teachers and Staff in Jinling Primary and Secondary Schools

Principal Wang Huanzhang Embezzles Public Funds and Deducts Salaries

Mediation by the Education Bureau Does Not Work

All Teachers and Staff Call on Various Groups for Assistance

The Jinling Primary and Secondary School on Hongkou Wuzhou Road in this city has a long history and the school's affairs are fairly developed. Unfortunately, this semester, due to the principal's deduction of salaries and the teachers' inability to obtain salaries, a trend has occurred. After mediation by the Education Bureau, a satisfactory result has not been obtained. The principal and teachers are likely to meet in court. The Shanghai News reporter believes that this matter is of great concern to people in the teaching field, and specially records the course of events as follows:

The school was originally named Gongdu Public School. The school has a long history. It was founded 36 years ago and was originally named Christian Public School. It was founded by the American Christian Association in the 24th year of the Guangxu period of the Qing Dynasty. In the 8th year of the Republic of China, Wang Huanzhang and others took over and renamed it Jinling No. 1 Public School. Later, it was renamed the Primary and Secondary School of the Jinling University Alumni Association. It is a school with a long history in Hongkou. The school's affairs are fairly developed. The chairman of the school board is Wu Dongchu, the vice chairman is Wei Wenhan, and the school board members are Tan Rongpu, Liu Jingwan, Liu Xuyuan, Hong Huanxiang, Wang Bingrong, Cui Shuzhu, Zhou Maofan, Wang Hongmo, Ren Yangui, and Hu Xiangquan. The principal is Wang Huanzhang, and the dean of teaching is Yang Geng.

Deduction of Salaries Triggers Trends: All of the school's soldiers Mao Rongzong, Shi Yunshi, Shi Hongru, Zheng Weirui, Chen Hongnian, Wang Bingrong, Chen Xingcheng, Guan Maojiang, Xu Zhusan, He Shaozhai, Wen Tianping, Gu Yuren, Li Huaibai, Zhu Damin and other more than 30 people, because the school principal Wang Huanzhang embezzled public funds and deducted salaries, repeatedly demanded payment, but did not pay them, so they jointly filed a complaint with the Municipal Education Bureau and the Municipal Party Department and other agencies, requesting assistance. The school authorities heard the news and on October 24 at 2 pm, Principal Wang, accompanied by Wei Wenhan, a representative of the school board, came to the school and claimed to the teachers and staff that salaries would be paid on November 1. The school was slightly relieved. On October 31, the principal suddenly forced each teacher and staff member to sign an illegal document before paying salaries. At that time, the teachers and staff refused to sign. The draft of the document is as follows: Dear Sir, the salary owed by Mr. Wang Huanzhang to me is ○○ yuan. I should seek compensation from Mr. Wang Huanzhang personally, and I will never ask the school board or the school to repay it. If the school's income and expenses are offset and there is a surplus, and the school board believes that my payment can be gradually compensated, regardless of whether it is a partial payment, the amount, or how it is allocated, all shall be decided by the school board, and I will not hold any objection. Furthermore, I will not transfer the rights of my payment to a third party. This letter is sent to the Jinling Primary and Secondary School Board for your reference.

The Education Authorities Have Mediated: After receiving the complaint, the Municipal Party Department and the Municipal Education Bureau sent personnel to investigate. The Education Bureau also sent Sun Shiju to convene representatives of the school board, the principal, and the teachers and staff to the Bureau on the 8th of last month to settle the matter. The school board did not attend that day, and Principal Wang Huanzhang fully represented the board. At that time, it was publicly decided that all outstanding salaries below 100 yuan would be paid in full, those between 100 yuan and 200 yuan would be paid 80%, and those above 200 yuan would be paid half, and the remaining arrears would be raised gradually, with the end of December this year as the deadline for full payment. Both parties accepted and had no objection. However, Principal Wang repeatedly delayed and did not comply. The teachers and staff petitioned the Education Bureau again, and the school only paid half a month's salary on the 10th of last month.

Calling on All Circles for Assistance Again: The school's teachers and staff felt that the school was insincere in paying the arrears and submitted a petition to the Party and government agencies and various education groups, stating that they were repeatedly requesting salaries but could not obtain them, and they were exhausted and their lives were at stake. They earnestly requested assistance to relieve the plight and save lives. The school teachers and staff are submitting the petition because the Jinling University Alumni Association Primary and Secondary School has been in arrears of salaries for several months (a total of 1,770 yuan and 43 cents as of October). They previously petitioned your association for relief and hoped that you would forward it to the Education Bureau to order the payment of salaries to maintain their lives. At the same time, the teachers and staff personally went to the Education Bureau to plead for assistance. They were all mediated by Mr. Sun Shiju of the Bureau. The teachers and staff respected the orders of their superiors and obeyed the guidance of the competent personnel. They still returned to the school with empty stomachs to perform their duties, consolidating the prestige of the Education Bureau, and they did not dare to be ignorant and engage in wasting the students' time. However, the school board and the principal did not take education seriously, relied on their power to bully others, and despised the Education Bureau. They spoke earnestly, but they ignored it. They even placed the lives of hard-working teachers at the mercy of the capitalists. Now, in the cold winter, the north wind is whistling, and they have no clothes and no food. Their lives are at stake. Not only can they not bear the responsibility of teaching, but they also cannot take care of the burden of their families. For this reason, they have no choice but to beg your association to investigate, take pity on their plight, and earnestly provide assistance and ask the Education Bureau to quickly order the school board and the principal to pay the salaries immediately to relieve the plight and save lives. They cannot express their gratitude enough. Sincerely,

Essays

Little Western Paradise

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter 5: Fawning and Flattery Meet the Lamp Illuminating, the Withered and Hungry Stomach Drives Makeup to Learn Elegance

Auntie Hu raised her chopsticks, not asking good or bad, and immediately ate several pieces of stir-fried leeks with shredded pork, which were truly fresh and salty. After eating a few bites, she couldn't put down her chopsticks. After biting two pieces of cornbread, she picked up a few strands of leeks and put them in her mouth to chew. Turning her head to see Yueying sitting listlessly on the side, staring blankly, she broke off a large piece of cornbread, stuffed it into her hand, and said with a smile, "Why are you just staring? He's inviting us to eat, so let's just eat. Even if we don't eat, we still have to appreciate his kindness." Yueying originally didn't want to eat, but she hadn't had enough to eat for two days. Now that she had something to fill her stomach in her hand, deliberately not eating would be too unfair to her own belly. Moreover, Auntie Hu was holding cornbread in her left hand and stir-fried leeks with shredded pork in her right, chewing with a clicking sound, and the flames of that appetite were almost spraying out from her seven orifices. She couldn't bear it, so she brought the cornbread to her mouth and first bit off a little corner to try. Although the thing was very rough, it was softened and made fragrant and delicious by the saliva in her mouth. Unconsciously, she sent the cornbread into her stomach. Seeing that she didn't have any cornbread in her hand, Auntie Hu broke off another piece and stuffed it into her hand, saying with a smile, "Since you've eaten, just keep eating." If Yueying hadn't touched the cornbread at all, she wouldn't have felt anything, but after her mouth was stained with food, she wanted to eat even more. So this time, when Auntie Hu stuffed the cornbread into her hand, she couldn't hesitate like before. She took it in her hand and stuffed it into her mouth. Before long, she finished what was in her hand. Following this trend, naturally, she wouldn't stop. In the end, she swept away everything that Little Ji had brought out. It was just that the canned pickled mustard tuber was too salty to finish, so Auntie Hu poured it out and wrapped it all up with the old paper on the table. Looking outside the door to see that no one was there, she put it in her pocket. (83)

Snippets

— (Nailing)

If peace could be obtained from prayer, then I don't think the wars that have occurred in this world would have happened!

Only those who can calmly deal with difficult obstacles without being at a loss can be said to be great people!

Remembering Hangzhou

— Bomin

Although I am very tired of city life, how can I return to the countryside? Thinking that life will ultimately not escape the circle of the city, I cannot help but forever remember the gentle and peaceful Hangzhou. Last night, my fellow villager Shen Banmei invited me to Zhiweiguan to taste the flavors of Hangzhou cuisine. Coincidentally, my younger brother came from Hangzhou, and at the dinner table, I also met Mr. Chen Junyi and Huang Xuchu, who had just played in Hangzhou. At that time, eating vinegar fish, water shield, and several other Hangzhou dishes, listening to the full-mouthed Hangzhou accent of the waiter, and talking about the various events in Hangzhou, I almost thought we were in between the Six Bridges and the Three Temples. Returning to my residence, I couldn't help but remember Hangzhou.

Speaking of Hangzhou, this place is truly worthy of people's joy and admiration. Just think, isn't there this sentence in ancient poems?

This is: "Directly take Hangzhou as Bianzhou."

This Bianzhou is the ancient Bianliang, which was once the capital of the country. That is enough to make people think that Hangzhou in the past was as magnificent as the hometown of emperors. Moreover, Hangzhou was also once the capital during the Southern Song Dynasty. And there is also a popular folk proverb: "Above there is heaven, below there are Suzhou and Hangzhou." Isn't this an ironclad annotation that Hangzhou is worthy of joy and admiration?

Hangzhou is truly like heaven; the most beautiful place in this place is the West Lake, and the mountains surrounding the lake are also very beautiful. In the mountains and on the lake, there are temples and monasteries everywhere, symbolizing the appearance of heaven. There are also small boats in the "Red Cliff Night Cruise" picture, and there are painted boats, truly occupying all the beautiful scenery of the world. I think if you are a famous writer, then the place to write manuscripts must be Hangzhou.

I used to live in Hangzhou. I remember that every time the weather was cool but not cold in the evening, I would always go to the Hubin Park area with Lifang without spending a penny, to relax. Sometimes, leaning on the railing and jumping into the distance, taking advantage of the setting sun, I would point out the peaks and laugh and talk about my ambition to buy a mountain and live in seclusion with her in the future. This dream is truly forever remembered in my heart.

I remember Hangzhou! Although when it comes to the typical city, Hangzhou is far inferior to Shanghai, and there is no atmosphere of foreign masters there. But fortunately, Hangzhou does not have these, which is why it is worthy of remembering.

The Temple of Literature in Early Winter

— Huang Yingdai

Autumn has already said goodbye to the world. When you step on the street and a gust of cold wind blows in your face, you will feel some cold air on your body. At the same time, the old trees on the side of the street have also been blown off a few yellow leaves, rolling on the ground with the wind. This is obviously the weather of early winter, right?

In Nanshi, if you have nothing to do, the only place to pass the time is probably only the Temple of Literature, right? In this early winter weather, when you step into the Temple of Literature, isn't everything still the same as usual? But the flowers in the Temple of Literature Park have withered, the grass has withered and yellowed, and except for some evergreen trees, the leaves of the trees have also fallen off and are almost bald. There is nothing as lively as autumn, right?

Among the friends who are touring the park here, no one came by car, everyone walked here, right? At most, only a few came by rickshaw. Therefore, when you walk to the park gate, you will experience that there is a kind of democratic meaning here. This park is not the exclusive property of a few idle classes!

On the grass that is about to wither, the slogans of the New Life Movement, "Understand Propriety and Righteousness" and "Know Shame," will immediately make you feel that you should be extra cautious here and not violate any prohibitions!

Look, on the sidewalk, people are walking in a continuous stream. The iron benches are full of men and women, and there is no empty seat left. In the Great Achievement Hall, scholars are admiring the relics of Confucius. The library is full of ambitious young people reading books and newspapers—this is a light description of a painting of the Temple of Literature in early winter.

— Yin Juan

Female Pedicurists

— Wang Shapa

It is said that female pedicurists are also one of the new female professions! Although this term is not very pleasant to hear and the job seems humble, it is not only easy to do but also quite profitable! Every day, they earn anywhere from four or five yuan to seven or eight yuan, which is comparable to the salary of a high-ranking employee. This is because their clients are all higher-class Western families. Chinese people would never patronize them. Their price per job is roughly one to two yuan. It is said that this skill, like hairdressing, requires hard work to learn, and also requires fluency in a foreign language.

In addition to pedicures, they also do manicures, but the money has to be given separately.

Here—on Shanzhong Road—female pedicurists can often be seen. The reason is that most of the residents in the tall Western-style houses are Japanese and Westerners, so female pedicurists are often seen.

When they go to offer their skills after being notified by the servant, long cheongsams and short coats are nothing special. Some even wear high heels and take chartered cars. They carry a handbag, and to those who don't know them, they must seem like female students or female doctors!

There is a female pedicurist named Chen who must be highly skilled and have a good business. She always earns more than ten yuan a day. She has a daughter who studies at a school on Haig Road and goes to school every day in a chartered car.

Chatter

From Writing to Plagiarism

— Huoxueming

Why do we write articles? It's a long story, but to put it simply: people cannot be without emotions, and since there are feelings, there must be a way to express them. When speaking with the mouth, it is called "speaking," and when writing with a pen, it is called "articles." And speaking, except for the phonograph, which can be preserved for centuries, cannot be passed on to later generations. Moreover, the phonograph was not invented before 1877. Since it was invented, no one has had the convenience of singing their "sorrows and joys" into a recording machine. Therefore, writing articles has become a social undertaking, with a strong influence on public consciousness. Stalin of Soviet Russia therefore said that writers are "the soul engineers of the whole people." Some even say that the French Revolution originated from Rousseau's thesis, and the transformation of Soviet Russian politics benefited from the novels of Turgenev and others. It can be seen that writing articles really has a dual meaning of natural expression and adapting to objective environmental needs.

What does the substance of "moaning without illness" contain? Therefore, the eight-legged essays and examination poems of the Qing Dynasty are worthless in modern times, while the Li Sao, which writes about a lifetime of melancholy, is still praised even though the words are difficult to understand. This is not to say that the rhetoric of the Li Sao is necessarily better than the works of the Qing Dynasty's court literati, but the difference lies in the fact that Qu Yuan had to write to express his loneliness and anger. In the examination hall, the examinees had no desires or thoughts in their hearts and reluctantly wrote eight-legged essays, adding a "given title" at the end, praising the emperor. May I ask, what value does this article have?

From this, we can know that writing articles must not be "empty talk." Things that are empty talk are just wax apples and paper-cut flowers, which cannot be chewed or smelled because they have no real life.

However, in this day and age, there are countless writers who write about different life experiences in different stages of consciousness. And there are also some pitifully clever people who consider themselves to be "writers" and rely on "selling articles for a living." Selling articles for money, and money for food, is originally a "noble occupation" in the eyes of gentlemen, but unfortunately, creating a noble occupation is not as easy as picking up mustard seeds. It is necessary to read a few books, walk a few miles, use your brain, and pick up a pen. When "inspiration strikes," pick up a pen and write, pouring out thousands of miles, only then can you be considered a writer. If you don't even have these skills, frowning and crying, unable to write a single word all day long, and you have to eat and wear clothes, then—then "plagiarism" comes!

The wind of plagiarism has existed since ancient times. However, the ancients were much cleverer after all. For example, the opening sentence of Du Fu's "Spring View," "The country is broken, but the mountains and rivers remain; in the spring city, the grass and trees are deep," is similar to Jing Shu's poem on the Ci'en Temple Pagoda in the Tang Dynasty, "The mountains and rivers of the Han country remain; the grass and trees are deep in the Qin mausoleum. The evening clouds stretch for thousands of miles, and there is no place without heartbreak." Lu You's "I wish to transform my body into a thousand billion, one plum blossom, one Lu You," seems to have been stolen from Liu Zongyuan's poem "Seeing the Mountains with Haochu and Sending to Relatives and Friends in the Capital," which says: "The sharp mountain by the sea is like the tip of a sword, and the sadness cuts the intestines everywhere in autumn. If I could transform my body into a thousand billion, I would scatter them on the peaks and look towards my hometown." However, this kind of plagiarism is limited to the method of chapters and sentences and still has the author's spirit in it. Perhaps they loved a certain line of someone's poem, treasured it in their hearts for a long time, and when they sang it themselves, they unconsciously melted it into their works, which is not worthy of criticism. As for the notebooks of the Ming and Qing Dynasties, which plagiarized each other, there are countless examples, but everyone can always, in a large paragraph of text, either reverse the facts, or insert other themes, or plagiarize the meaning but not the words, using various methods to avoid being recognized as "plagiarism" at a glance.

It is ridiculous that there are now many "writers" who unceremoniously copy the articles of their contemporaries in the same way, crown them with their own names, and send them to newspapers or magazines for publication. The inner meaning of this, if it is not to cheat for稿费 (payment), to support one's own life, it must be to deliberately make trouble for the editors, thinking that deceiving and selling is precisely mocking the editors' lack of knowledge. (In fact, there are so many Chinese publications, how can editors browse all of them and how can they never forget after reading them?) The former is hateful, but understandable, while the latter is a hooligan's trick, and the sin is unforgivable. However, the exposure of plagiarists and the cancellation of payments are seen on publications from time to time, and the same infamous events continue to occur!

To purify the literary world, it is undoubtedly necessary to eradicate these "plagiarists"—regardless of whether the reason for their plagiarism is for survival.

It was heard in the second half of the market that the gold market fell back and the market was tired.

American cotton also followed suit, rising by twenty points. The reason for the trend of Indian cotton was that the cotton growing area there was hit by heavy rains, and the source in the market was lacking. Japanese merchants bought in and rose sharply. Chang Feng and Da Fu bought in one or two "man" loads, making the trading floor tight. Each month rose by 0.6 to 0.75 jiao. The market situation changed when it reached the second or third session in the afternoon, with the gold price falling back slightly. According to a message from a certain cotton industry organization, Indian cotton may fall back by two or three rupees tomorrow, so the heart of the people was slightly relaxed. Each month fell by 0.05 to 0.1, 0.15, and 0.2 jiao. The total volume traded for the day was 143,000 loads. Records of the Faint Scent of Imperial Incense

— Original by Princess Der Ling, translated by Qin Shouou

Besides this large glass case, there was another very small glass case, inside which were two items unrelated to the portrait in the case; but they were equally precious. One was a jade ring, which the Empress Dowager said was often used by Emperor Qianlong during his lifetime, and the other was a very delicate and smooth snuff bottle, also carved from the most brightly colored jade. These were all items of relatively high value. Next in line were many musical instruments. Because Qianlong was a versatile monarch, proficient in Qin (zither), chess, calligraphy, and painting; his attainment in music was particularly high. These musical instruments had been personally played by him for a long time, so they were also considered a part of the very memorable relics.

Probably because this incomparably wise emperor was very fond of collecting porcelain during his lifetime, most of his relics were various kinds of porcelain, occupying almost eight-tenths of a large hall. Among these porcelains, many were cloisonné and bronze-colored. Those who knew the goods knew that they were rare精品s that were not easy to find. If they had been treasured all the way to the present, their value must have been very considerable!

That is all there is of Qianlong's relics! Although we all used a particularly respectful attitude and appreciated them for a long time, because Qianlong was indeed very far away from us, we could no longer, after viewing the relics, feel much sincere and earnest remembrance of him. Not only were we like this, but even the Empress Dowager herself probably did not have any deep feelings; although in fact she was the direct successor to Qianlong's authority, and she often liked to mention this talented ancestor, seemingly feeling very honored, but in her heart, he really had no place! Free Talk

A Differing Opinion Presented to Mr. Wu Liping

— Mengjia

In his article "Differences in Literature and Life," Mr. Liping presented two "different" opinions on Mr. Huanping's "Literature and Life," but his so-called "differences" were merely restating the latter's views. Let us look at Mr. Liping's "differing opinions": "First, I disagree with the idea that "a person as a poet" participating in real life can truthfully capture any image and express the truth and essence of life." The reason is that "a person "as a poet" is somewhat different from a person after all, and their attitude towards participating in real life is also different, so their life content is also different. At this time, if what the poet captures and expresses belongs to the scope of human beings, then its truthfulness is very questionable." Gorky and Balzac were not "people as poets" but participated in real life as "people," so "if you want to express the truth and essence of life, you must first live with the attitude of a person; only "direct" life can touch the truth and essence of life," otherwise, "even if the attitude towards real life is not a bystander's game, at least it is using real life as a means." (Note: This sentence seems to have a problem; it is probably referring to using visiting real life as a means) The examples are Tao Yuanming, who "returned to the field to become a farmer," and Chen Mengjia, who "participated in the Shanghai War to find poetry materials."

The point that Mr. Liping emphasizes above is the so-called "direct life," and this "direct life" is exactly the opposite of the so-called "observation-based life." We ask writers to immerse themselves in real life and capture their own images from this fertile field of reality. This statement is precisely aimed at the current general writers who limit their writing to "trivial matters around them." Emphasizing the importance of real-life experience in the production process of works does not mean obliterating the importance of the writer's talent, that is, the so-called "artistic expression." The problem must be clarified so that the discussion will not go astray. Mr. Liping has somewhat distorted the original author's opinion on this point. We say "direct real life" precisely because "observational real life" often makes people only see the surface of life and cannot delve into the core of life, so the result is often "untrue" in expression. But it is not to say that "indirect" or "observation-based methods" are completely undesirable. A writer's writing theme is complicated. If every aspect of life requires a "personal experience," then he must either be "immortal" or simply drop the pen, which can be said to be a joke.

When we say direct life, that is, asking writers to immerse themselves in objective real life, we are precisely asking writers to liberate themselves from the small room, or—if they are more wealthy, then it should be said that they are in a western-style building or villa—from their own narrow real life. Although "going to the crossroads" can also observe some truth about real life, which is certainly good; however, we also have the right to ask him to do better: to go to the countryside and factories. This also means that "it is always better for artists to delve into the actual life of the people than to mix in the so-called literary world and do nothing (should add a sentence: and do some "leisurely" things)." That makes it impossible for him to produce any great works at present, but this possibility is always greater than continuing to be careless, because in this real-life process, his image storage will be enriched along with his life experience. At the same time, real life is diverse and complex; therefore, in art, we need not only tragic marches but also the era's eulogies that can profoundly embody the torment and sorrow of the soul of the dwarfs in the era's boiler.

Oh dear, I've gone too far.

Mr. Liping's first mistake is that he regards the writer's participation in real life and the indirect observation of life as the same thing. At the same time, because of his mechanical view of "people as poets" and "people in general"—only seeing the differences between the two and obliterating the sameness between the two—he derives the erroneous conclusion that "people as poets participating in real life cannot truthfully capture typical images," and even thinks that "literary figures are never created; they are just people of real life, and their works are just direct life experiences. They do not live in order to produce great works. If there are great literary works in China, they must not be works of the "people as poets and novelists" type." And his most brilliant, and also most erroneous, conclusion: "Literary figures are not created, which is equivalent to not being able to create literary figures." It is also based on his erroneous point of view. He flatly denies the future of general writers at the current stage. Literary figures are not created but are treasures that fall from the sky. Then, the requirement to enrich the writer's real life should be a useless act, and the work of attracting and guiding general writers at present is also superfluous. According to this, then we should no longer have any hope for general writers who do not have a fulfilling life, and if these people do not automatically change their careers, then they must be cursed to the end!

Kukul River

— Shidai

Stars are gone, the moon has fallen, why can't I see my beloved brother? Ma ta yi ma o, die ma yi ya yo, my eyes are swollen from crying, I don't sleep, eat, or drink.

Ai Li Gale girl, sitting on the green grass, holding a white, chubby little lamb. Frowning and looking up at the sky, she rubbed the lamb's back weakly and sang again and again in a sharp, thin voice.

The sound of the Kukul River flowing from afar, Ai Li Gale sang for a while and then closed her mouth, listening quietly to the murmuring water, penetrating her heart, penetrating the depths of her heart.

The sun moved onto the grass, onto the green Shabuer Plain. Horses neighed. Sheep jumped. The joyful cattle, like birds in a cage, staggered east and west. Camels lay motionless, sunbathing.

Worry deeply branded Ai Li Gale's brow.

——Zha Ke Balu brother!

Zha Ke Balu's shadow flickered before her eyes again, what a strong young man, copper shoulders and iron arms, who wouldn't like him! A purplish face hiding a smile, a pair of lively eyes, spraying charming light. When he came back from hunting in Mount Jibatu with a gun on his back, he walked past Ai Li Gale's yurt with a hey hey mouth, and Ai Li Gale peeked out, watching until Zha Ke Balu walked into the yurt before she dragged her heavy feet back to the yurt in a dispirited manner.

Ai Li Gale was silent, and after a while, she picked up her head and looked at the livestock lying, calling, and jumping on the grass.

Anxiety burned in her heart, she angrily pushed away the lamb in her arms, frantically tore at her hair, stood up and walked for a while, and then sat down and dug at the grass roots with her hands.

In a blink of an eye, Zha Ke Balu stood in front of her, with a gun on his back and a fox in his left hand. His eyes shot at Ai Li Gale's face, and Ai Li Gale felt hot all over, unable to speak.

Zha Ke Balu bent down to rub the sleeping little sheep:

—Miss Ai Li Gale, please give me this sheep!

As soon as he finished speaking, he laughed loudly, and Ai Li Gale also knew clearly that he was joking, but she didn't say anything.

Ai Li Gale picked up a mud lump and threw it at the sheep on the opposite side, deliberately throwing it diagonally at Zha Ke Balu. Zha Ke Balu walked over with a smile and grabbed Ai Li Gale's hand.

—What a fierce young lady!

Her face turned hot, and she lowered her head.

After a long time, Ai Li Gale said softly:

—Are you willing to be with me?

Zha Ke Balu nodded with a smile on his face.

—I'll take you to see the water of the Kukul River!

There were no clouds in the sky, the sun became more and more coquettish, and the wind seemed to have been defeated and could not blow at all. Zha Ke Balu dragged Ai Li Gale, and Ai Li Gale called out to the flock of sheep.

Walking, walking, walking happily.

The water of the Kukul River was as clear as a mirror, and the green grass covered the river embankment, and the sunlight splashed on the water, emitting a glittering light. The two banks were a vast plain like a flat green felt.

Zha Ke Balu held Ai Li Gale's hand and paced along the river bank, and the light of the river reflected on their faces, making their purplish complexions extraordinarily charming.

The white flock of sheep was jumping, constantly moving on the green grass. The sunlight dyed the grass, dyed the flock of sheep, dyed the Kukul River, and dyed Zha Ke Balu's eyes.

The warm climate only attracted sleepy bugs, drilling into people's bodies and into livestock. A burst of laziness came up, which would make you listless, groggy, and your eyes dry and astringent. You would only feel comfortable after taking a nap.

The two people sat on the ground, not speaking to each other, you looked at me, I looked at you.

Ai Li Gale's heart suddenly jumped.

She discovered a secret in the flock of sheep.

A ram and a ewe were sleeping side by side! How comfortable!

Lowering her head with shyness, her face turned green with fire, her heart was thumping and thumping, and her whole body seemed to be boiling water.

After a while, she tried hard to suppress this heat, but she could not calm her beating heart.

——There was a day when I was with Zha...

Zha Ke Balu watched the changes in their expressions. She patted her heart, and her face showed a longing expression.

X X X X

At some point, a team of people and horses came from behind Mount Jibatu and walked along this side of the Kukul River. Zha Ke Balu stared at the group of people and horses. Within a hundred steps, he already understood that they were the soldiers under Che Khan, who were in charge of the herdsmen on the Shabuer Plain. When this team of people and horses stopped in front of them, Zha Ke Balu recognized that it was Sa Qi Gan, the head of the soldiers under Che Khan, leading fifty or sixty people and horses. Displaying their power and flaunting their might, they all dismounted, and a fierce look hung on the face of each soldier.

Ai Li Gale's heart was pounding in her mouth, she hugged Zha Ke Balu's waist with both hands, closed her eyes, and almost didn't dare to breathe.

Zha Ke Balu held up the fox with both hands:

—A gift for King Sa Qi Gan!—

Sa Qi Gan didn't say anything, nor did he take the fox. He stepped forward and dragged Ai Li Gale, asking with a smirk:

—Did he come to steal your sheep?

—No! He is a good person.

Ai Li Gale was shivering all over, and her jaw felt a little stiff.

A man in a yellow jacket walked to Sa Qi Gan's side and whispered something in Sa Qi Gan's ear.

Sa Qi Gan smiled hey hey, with a knife hidden in his smile.

With a snap, Sa Qi Gan's whip landed on Zha Ke Balu's body.

—Robber!

Ai Li Gale's heart felt like it was being stabbed with a knife!

—Girl, come with me.

Sa Qi Gan patted Ai Li Gale's shoulder. He was fascinated by this girl.

The whiplashes rang one after another on Zha Ke Balu's body, no one could bear it. Zha Ke Balu couldn't bear it any longer and lifted up his gun.

Bang!

Sa Qi Gan fell to the ground in response, followed by:

Bang! Bang! Bang……… The gunshots rang continuously, and in a burst of chaos, the horses jumped, the sheep scattered, and Ai Li Gale and Zha Ke Balu lost their lives in the gunshots!

The green plain, the flat grass, was painted with bright red blood, the sun was spraying heat, and the fishy stench swelled up.

A large group of soldiers carried Sa Zhengshi's body onto the horse, drove the sheep, and drove the camels, with sorrow smeared on everyone's face.

The water of the Kukul River flowed gurglingly, passing through the plain, a green grassland, inlaid with a winding white band.

A burst of crying came from afar, not knowing whose livestock the group of soldiers was shooting.

A Glimpse of Yangon

— Liu Ming

I live upstairs in a small teahouse on Maung Khine Street. There is nothing to do, and few people come to chat. Most of my lonely time is spent idly gazing out the window and reading a worn-out book.

I have completely forgotten what the book said, but the various pictures of life seen from the window still remain clearly with distinct outlines and colors.

Every morning, along with the tender yellow sunlight, a Burmese monk slowly walking down the street appears before my eyes. He is bald, barefoot, wearing yellow robes, and holding a black lacquer bowl. When he arrives on the street in front of the teahouse, he walks up to the steps in front of a Chinese family's door diagonally across from me.

This is a rather wealthy Chinese family, which can be seen from the exquisite furniture in the room upon entering. The Burmese monk does not stand on the steps to beg for alms, but walks in as if he were coming home, sits down in a chair, motionless and silent, like a Buddha statue that has not sat cross-legged. A woman in a colorful dress immediately walks out of the room, looking neither Chinese nor Burmese (this is a woman born to a Chinese father and a Burmese mother). She takes off the slippers on her feet to the monk, kneels down, and kowtows respectfully before taking the monk's bowl. Then, she puts on her slippers and walks inside. After a while, when she brings out the bowl filled with rice and vegetables, she takes off her slippers again and kneels down to kowtow. The monk, on the other hand, sits there ignoring her, takes the bowl, and leaves silently.

During the day, I occasionally see compatriots in disheveled clothes, with short hair and unclean heads, standing on the steps in front of the door of the family that the monk visited, murmuring words that probably ask for help to return home. A man with a cigarette hanging from the corner of his mouth and wearing a Chinese-style short outfit appears in the door, raises his fat hand, and waves unhappily, then disappears inside. Next, a thin Indian servant comes out, making a fuss with scolding and roaring gestures. Thereupon, the beggar who is adrift in a foreign country walks down the steps dejectedly, and turns back to scold the Indian man angrily:

"You black devil!"

During the Lunar New Year, the thin Indian servant hangs a large Chinese flag on the door of this family, fluttering under the eaves. Firecrackers that look like flashes of electricity are also set off in large numbers. When I get up the next morning and look, the street is covered with red paper flowers that are more than an inch thick. Before, I suspected from the impression that they had probably naturalized as Burmese, but at this time, I realized that they were indeed Chinese.

Tomorrow (10)

— (Written by Joseph Conrad) Translated by Wu Xiangyu

Captain Hagberd came a step nearer, leaning forward, resting on his spade handle. "Go your way," he said angrily, and yet timorously too, for he was ever frightful of being made a fool of. Every state of mind, even madness, has its equilibrium based upon self-esteem. Disturb that, and you disturb misery; and Captain Hagberd lived amongst a system of unfathomable ideas, which made him feel that somebody was trying to jeer out his pain. Yes, other people's jeers were terrible. They suggested something wrong; but what? He couldn't tell: the stranger was clearly jeering—was at it on purpose in coming there. And the worse was doing it in the street, though he had never been so worked upon before.

The stranger, unaware of the nearness, of the elderly man's bent figure resting forward on his spade, said sternly, "I am not encroaching on any one, am I? I suspect your advertisement is somehow not quite right. Suppose you let me come inside."

"You come inside!" old Hagberd whispered, in extreme consternation.

"I could give you some really truthful news of your son—and the very last, if you care to listen."

"No," cried Hagberd loudly. He began pacing to and fro, shouldering his spade, waving the other hand aimlessly. "Here's a fellow—a jeering fellow, who says something is not quite right. I have news got more than you know. I've got all the news I want. I had it years ago—years ago—years ago—quite enough to wait for tomorrow. Let you come inside, indeed! What would Harry say?"

Bessie Carvil's form made a black patch upon the parlour window; then the door clicked, appearing before the other cottage, and every part of her was black, only above her head was something white. The men's voices beginning all at once speaking outside the door, (she had heard them before inside the house) gave her such an emotion, she could scarcely produce any sound.

Captain Hagberd looked as if he was trying to find a way out of a cage. His feet sank in the quagmire he had upturned. The holes in the debased lawn almost made him stumble. He blindly rushed to the paling.

"Here's comfort!" said the man at the door, sternly, stretching forth his arm, seizing his sleeve. "Somebody has been at you. Hullo! what clothes are these you wear? Good God, it's stiff canvas." He laughed. "Well, you are a figure!"

Captain Hagberd disengaged himself and began retreating abjectly. "Leastways now," he said in a tone of dispirited conviction.

"Something has come over him!" The stranger appealed to Bessie with an earnest request for explanation, as if they had been extremely intimate. "I didn't want to upset the old man." He lowered his voice as if he had known her for years. "I happened to step into a barber's round the corner—two pence for a shave—and they told me he was a bit of a figure. The old boy has made a perfect figure of himself."

Supplement to the Local Section of the Shen Bao

Casual Remarks

Photo of Pu Yi

— Cow

Speaking of photographs, they are my favorite gift from heaven. For example, photos of prostitutes, photos of dancers, photos of movie stars, and even photos of naked women. If they are taken well and the faces are pretty, I will buy them and nail them to the wall, looking at them day and night, which I find very interesting.

Because photographs are realistic. If I haven't seen a woman before, seeing her photo is like seeing the woman herself. So, hanging a woman's photo on the wall feels like living with that woman. This is not me "daydreaming." I think there must be many "daydreamers" like me in the world.

Not only are photos of women lovely, but also photos of landscapes, or photos of ancient people and objects, are lovely. There are many famous mountains and scenic spots in the world, and we often can't go to enjoy them. But seeing photos is like having been there. Also, rare treasures and famous historical figures, which cannot be collected or seen in reality, can be seen through photos, as if they have been collected or met in person.

In addition, I also thoroughly like photos of important people. Because I cannot climb up to important people or get close to them, hanging their photos on the wall is like having a "heart-to-heart talk in a small room" or "sharing a conversation at the table" with them. Involuntarily, I feel larger, more generous, and more ambitious.

There is another type of photo that I also like, which is the record of the Northeast Volunteer Army's resistance against Japan. Since "September 18th," the four provinces have fallen. The patriotic men and women of the Northeast do not hesitate to sacrifice their lives, fighting the Japanese and traitors hand-to-hand in the white mountains and black waters. I truly admire this patriotic spirit "with my whole body prostrate on the ground." Seeing these photos makes my blood boil. So, these photos are also lovely.

The most unsightly photos are those of Zhong Kui catching ghosts, or of robbers being sentenced to death and executed by firing squad. They are disgusting to look at. Because these photos cause both fear and hatred. If I see such photos, I will tear them up and burn them, destroying the evidence, and never let them leave any impression.

What is Pu Yi? He is a puppet of the Japanese, used by the Japanese as a tool to deceive the world. But he can't deceive the 30 million people of the Northeast Provinces, nor can he deceive the eyes and ears of people all over the world. Now, the pseudo-Ministry of Education wants to implement slave education. In order to numb the people of the Northeast Provinces, they recently ordered the pseudo-Ministry of Education to distribute photos of Pu Yi, the puppet who performed the ugly drama when he usurped the throne, to all primary and secondary schools in Manchuria, to be hung in the auditoriums and classrooms. "Who am I deceiving? Am I deceiving Heaven?"

I think although the four Northeast provinces are lost, the hearts of the people of the four Northeast provinces are not lost. Seeing such a puppet photo will only make them feel more ashamed of losing their country and more disgusted with the Japanese's tricks to deceive the people of the Northeast Provinces, thus further arousing their determination to resist Japan. Hanging such photos is actually keeping a memorial of national subjugation for the 30 million people of the Northeast, and it cannot be said to be a very beneficial trick.

Therefore, the same photo can evoke different feelings. Some people feel good when they see a photo, while others feel disgusted. Some may not directly show disgust, but the disgust is indirectly reflected and continuously exposed. Therefore, people with good judgment cannot erase or deceive the truth, justice, and fairness. Hanging Pu Yi's photo in schools may not be a tool to stimulate people's resistance. "Let them hang it."

Sympathy

— TT

One winter night, the north wind was howling, and snowflakes were floating in the air like cotton. The earth was eerily quiet. I hid in the house, tightly closing the windows and doors, sitting by the stove.

I never expected Lao Li to come to my place at this time. His face was flushed red by the wind, and his nose was running. I thought he would walk straight to the stove to warm himself up, but he stood still at the door, which was wide open. So I said:

"Close the door, it's quite cold."

The door was closed immediately, but he still stood there woodenly.

"Hey, what are you standing there for?" I said, standing up.

Only then did he step closer to the stove, reaching out to warm his hands, silently.

I stared at him in surprise. I was afraid he was having a nervous breakdown.

Suddenly, he squeezed my hand with effort and said very seriously:

"Lao Mu, shouldn't people have sympathy for each other?"

"Of course they should. For example, in such cold weather, if I don't even have a thin blanket, would you just watch me freeze to death while you have three or four quilts on your bed?"

"That's good, please come with me to my house for a moment." He jumped up and shouted loudly.

"It's freezing, what would I do at your house?"

"See my house." He faced the door and forcefully dragged my hand.

There was no choice but to put on a big coat and walk with him down the street.

The wind rushed against us in gusts, and my face stung a bit. I lowered my head and walked with big strides, as if in a long-distance race.

The whole road was deserted, with only the two of us. Snow covered our bodies. Occasionally, one or two cars sped past us, and Lao Li cursed madly:

"Damn! Sitting in the car themselves, watching others get sprinkled with snow, they have no sympathy."

"Damn sympathy, they don't care if you freeze to death." My teeth chattered as I spoke.

"Hahaha!" Lao Li waved his hands in the air.

My heart trembled. "Lao Li must be having a nervous breakdown," I thought. When we reached the entrance of his apartment, he searched all over his clothes and pockets, but couldn't find the key. He pounded on the door anxiously. The landlady's helper was probably fast asleep, because it took a long time for the door to crack open.

"Damn, sleeping so comfortably, making people stand at the door... they have no sympathy." He started up the stairs, cursing as he went.

In his room, I found that the quilt on the bed was gone. I thought he had taken it to the pawnshop, and I asked with a smile:

"Lao Li, did you send the quilt to the poor people's bank?"

He opened the drawer, took out a slip of paper, and asked me to look at it. It read:

"Lao Li, heaven told me to steal your quilt, please forgive me! Your friend C."

"Lao Chen? That's outrageous, he's afraid of the cold, doesn't he think others are afraid of the cold? Go get it back from him," I said angrily.

Lao Li patted me on the shoulder, laughed, and then said:

"People should have sympathy for each other!"

Page 20

City Night

— Ye Fei

Eleven o'clock struck. Coming out of the Grand Theatre after seeing "My Fair Lady," I squeezed through the crowd at the entrance, took a long breath, straightened my collar, and walked along the cement sidewalk, tapping my toes on the ground to an off-rhythm beat, while calculating in my mind which road to take.

The neon lights on the store signs were glaring at the pedestrians, and the "big sale" banners in front of the shops drooped listlessly. People were slithering through the streets as if mad. One after another, sleek new Austin and Chevrolet cars crawled along the asphalt spine of the road. The tallest and grandest cubist buildings stood quietly in the sky, their peaks touching the firmament. The biting cold wind stirred up the dust on the ground. I couldn't help but shiver, shrinking my head desperately into my collar.

With a lonely heart, I wandered aimlessly along the road. The nightingales of the street were singing mournful songs!

— Young master! Gentleman! Give a copper coin to a poor person, let me buy half a bowl of porridge!

— Sir! It's so cold, walking in the wind, why not come to my house and sit for a while!

Caught off guard by this, I was startled. I twisted my body abruptly, broke free from their hands, ran a few steps, and mechanically turned my head to glance at them, seeing them grinning foolishly at me, no, it was an unnatural bitter smile!

Passing in front of a dance hall, the melodious music inside captivated my soul. A young couple twirled out of the door, arm in arm, shoulder to shoulder. Making a turn, they slipped into an ice cream shop.

Walking with a waltz-like gait, speaking with the flavor of a "dancing partner song," wearing a jade-green cheongsam, with a narrow waist, a pair of well-developed breasts, quivering in front of her chest, and a charming smile always hanging on the corners of her mouth. That teasing sensuality! Even an old monk would be tempted to return to the secular world.

By then I had strolled to another road, a road so deserted it was like a dead street. Here I couldn't see women's smiles, nor could I hear the songs of Ramona, only two or three rickshaw pullers, dragging empty rickshaws, wandered listlessly through the street.

However, at the same time, on another road, one after another motorcycle was revving its engine, with several "beep! beep! beep!" roars, carrying these dance-weary and drunken gentlemen, ladies, young masters, and young ladies back home.

Fingernails

— Lu Yinquan

Late autumn, a season as melancholy as lilac, a season most suitable for sitting quietly alone. There is no dazzling sunlight, and the gentle wind seems afraid to hurt people's delicate skin, only softly caressing. At this time, it is best not to browse books, you know? Books are a north wind that messes up a tranquil heart. If you are not used to it, you can smoke a mild cigarette. As for me, I am used to sitting quietly like this. I often put my fingers in my mouth and slowly grind the sharp corners of my nails with my teeth. In the grinding of my nails, I can happily let so much time slip by. This is indeed the greatest comfort for me.

Today, a late autumn afternoon as melancholy as lilac, I sat down by the dilapidated south window, ready to admire my fingers again. But when I pulled up my fingers, I was surprised. How come the pink curtex on my nails has faded? I felt a little depressed.

You know, why should I be depressed? This is pink Curtex, applied by my wife before I left home. At that time, I was lying on a rattan chair, habitually putting my fingers in my mouth, timidly fearing the approaching taste of separation. My wife floated in from outside and saw my hands, she said:

— Look, your fingers are so dirty, and you still put them in your mouth.

She took my hands and caressed them with affection. Caress them more, I thought, the moment of separation will arrive in an instant. But she didn't seem to feel anything and was still very happy!

— Let me wash them for you, and add some Curtex, okay?

Without calling the maid, my wife brought the washbasin herself. After the clear water had completely washed away the dirt between my nails, she took pink nail polish and applied it stroke by stroke. Watching her green onion-like slender fingers move slowly, I had never been so happy.

When leaving this gentle hometown, my wife said with some sadness:

— May this Curtex serve as a souvenir of our honeymoon! But now, it has only been a few days since I came here, and the nail polish that serves as a souvenir has faded like this, how can people not feel sad?

The setting sun has already been carried away by the returning birds, and I am still sitting blankly, staring at my fingernails. Have I lost a soft dream? I do not know. Only my mind is a little dazed. From now on, I will not admire my fingernails anymore, because they will give me sour memories. So I put my hands down, stood up, and ran to the gatehouse to check the mail.

I hope that in the big pile of letters in the gatehouse, there is a letter with a familiar, delicate handwriting.

Amateur Mailbox

Statement Regarding "One Dollar for Three Days"

Editor:

The article "One Dollar for Three Days" published in the Amateur Mailbox the other day is slightly inconsistent with the facts, so I must make a statement to you.

Zhu Fumin is seventeen years old this year, and his height is the same as an adult, so he does not seem to be considered a child. When Mr. Zhu received the notice to come to our store, he stated that "he would try it for three days first, and if both parties agreed after three days, he would find a guarantor and be officially hired." But Mr. Zhu did not report this to his family, which caused a misunderstanding by Mr. Zhu's mother and brother, which of course our store cannot be responsible for.

However, Mr. Zhu's mother suddenly came to our store to make a scene on the evening of the day after the three days. Although our store explained to her the current application rules and that we had said "try it for three days first," she refused to listen and insisted that our store was cheating and slippery. It took about half an hour before she left.

Washing silverware is a task that our store needs to do every day. What Mr. Zhu wiped that day was not dozens of silver shields, but several silver cups. The silver cups were originally as shiny as mirrors, and only needed to wipe off some fingerprints and dust from the boxes. Mr. Zhu said that he had small blisters on his fingers from wiping, but Mr. Yu, who is now officially hired by our store, has been wiping for more than half a month and has not found any blisters. This is really strange.

The reason why Mr. Zhu was not hired, our store thinks it is unnecessary to explain further for Mr. Zhu's sake. In short, he is not suitable for our business, so we fulfilled the "try it for three days" agreement and dismissed Mr. Zhu, which of course cannot be said to be our store's mistake. Please accept my best wishes.

Sincerely,

Guanghua Optical Company

National Studies

Lady Wang Bingmei's Tang Poetry

Hua Xing (1260) 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM

Looking at the Wilderness by Du Fu

West Mountain's white snow becomes three-tenths of the borderland; South Shore's clear river flows to the ten-thousand-mile bridge.

Within the seas, the winds and dust separate me from my brothers; At the edge of the sky, tears and sorrow burden my solitary self from afar.

I can only offer my declining years to my many ailments; I have not contributed even a drop in return to the wise dynasty.

Mounting my horse, I leave the suburbs, often straining my eyes; I cannot bear to see human affairs growing more desolate day by day.

Hearing of the Recovery of Henan and Hebei by the Official Army by Du Fu

Suddenly, from beyond the sword gate, news arrives of the recovery of Hebei; At first hearing, tears of joy filled my clothes.

Turning to look at my wife and children, where is their worry? Casually rolling up my books, I am wild with joy.

In the bright daylight, I must sing and indulge in wine; With youth as my companion, it is good to return home.

Then, following the Ba Gorge, I will pass through the Wu Gorge; Then I will descend to Xiangyang, heading towards Luoyang.

Climbing High by Du Fu

The wind is swift, the sky is high, monkeys howl in sorrow; On the islet, the water is clear, the sand is white, birds fly into the distance.

Boundless fallen leaves rustle down; An endless long river rolls on.

Ten thousand miles away, grieving for autumn, I am always a guest; A hundred years of age, plagued by many illnesses, I climb alone.

Hardships and bitterness, I hate my frost-covered temples; Frustrated and dejected, I have newly stopped my cup of turbid wine.

Ascending the Tower by Du Fu

Flowers near the tall tower wound the heart of the traveler; In ten thousand regions, there are many difficulties in this ascent.

The spring colors of the Jin River come from heaven and earth; The floating clouds of Jade Mountain transform ancient and modern times.

The North Star court will never change; The bandit invaders of West Mountain must not encroach.

Pitiable that since coming here, I have only visited temples; As dusk falls, I will idly recite the Liangfu Song.
