Shen Bao Local Supplement - Film Special Issue

The Near Reality of Kay Francis's Loss of Sight (Part 2)

— Mi Ji

"Since the doctor diagnosed that Kay Francis's eyes were burned, he had to operate. His method of surgery was to cut away the burned, transparent cornea because after the cornea was burned, it had already wrinkled and become dry and hard. So I waited until 'Hell's Angels' was finished and immediately went for the operation. The pain of the operation, of course, goes without saying. Since the operation, I have worn dark glasses almost every day for eleven months, waiting for my eyes to slowly grow a new membrane. The doctor absolutely forbade me from reading or using my eyes much during this nearly one year, except for the necessary short periods. 'Hell's Angels' was completed in November 1930. Less than six months later, the company sent me to perform everywhere. Of course, I couldn't always wear black glasses when I was on stage. But she kept her dark glasses on until she went on stage, and then took them off. As soon as she came off stage, she put them back on. But when she was on stage, the lights were shining up into her eyes, which was as painful as being pricked with needles. So every time I came off stage, my eyes were as red as blood, and tears streamed down. So I hurriedly applied some pain-relieving medicine, closed my eyes and rested until the second time I went on stage. But sometimes, I was rushing around, appearing on stage five or six times a day. There were also many local officials and important people who had to be met in person. It was really very painful."

Indeed, the pain suffered by the eyes can be said to be the most difficult of all kinds of pain in the various parts of the body, which all of us who have suffered from eye diseases know. And because the physical problem affects the mental pain, it is also the most severe with the eyes. In the past three or four years, Kay Francis has felt the danger of going completely blind at any time. So, what kind of pain she has suffered in her nerves can be imagined. But she, a brave woman, did not tell anyone, nor did she blame anyone. She said, "Many times, I really wanted to tell people about it. Because many friends saw me and waved to me from afar, but I couldn't see them at all. People thought I was arrogant. In fact, I didn't know at all. My eyes could go blind at any time because they are the most delicate part of the body, and even a small irritation can cause big problems. At that time, my eyes were like being on a plane flying through the clouds. Sometimes I could see very clearly, and sometimes my vision was blurred. Once blurred, it could last for an hour or several days, and then suddenly it would brighten up again. The time I was most afraid of was when a film was about to be finished because I was filming every day, and my eyesight was getting worse day by day. By the last few days, I was almost completely blind, but the work could not be stopped."

So when she finally got out of danger, her happiness can be imagined. She said, "That kind of joy cannot be described in words. You can imagine it slowly. First of all, I thought about how happy my mother would be when I told her what the doctor had told me, once and twice. I knew that she was worried about me even more than I was worried about myself. That was certainly one of the reasons why Kay suffered great pain but refused to say it.) My mother often told me not to make any more films, otherwise, I would not be able to save my eyes. But I didn't listen to her and insisted on continuing. I knew that if I really went blind, I would be too sorry for my mother. Secondly, I didn't dare to mention this to the company, for fear that they would force me to stop working. I also thought of many things that I enjoyed doing, but for the sake of my eyes, I couldn't do or do them often for many years. First of all, now I can read the books that I bought a long time ago but haven't opened yet. Secondly, I can watch as many movies as I like without being limited to a few movies that I have to watch. In short, it's like the beginning of a new life, the beginning of an unrestricted life. That is such a happy thing, you go imagine it!" (The End)

Film Review

Review of (Rebirth Affinity)

— Ling He

Journal of A Crime

—Nanjing—

From a new perspective, this film is an old-fashioned work in any case. However, the playwright or author is very cinematic, expressing their old ideas.

Yes, there is no new content needed by the times here; there is only the art of old ideas or the savoring of human relationships. We have seen many such works in movies and literature, and people often feel pleasant or sad to varying degrees.

Here, the playwright emphasizes the sadness of women who are old and losing their beauty. When they lose their husband's love, they often use their entire lives to win their husband's love. Therefore, Fang Shu (played by Rose Crichton) risked her life to kill her rival in love. But people always have a conscience - at least old-fashioned artists often seize the treasure of conscience to illuminate their works. Therefore, under the condemnation of conscience, Fang Shu went to confess several times, although her capital crime of murder had already been taken over by a kind-hearted and chivalrous bandit.

After that, the playwright was unwilling to have a female protagonist who had fully won people's sympathy for a murderer be sentenced to death, and also wanted to give her a perfect ending. After she had suffered a lot of torment for love, she then made her use her good conscience to save a child's life, resulting in her own injury. Eventually, she suffered nerve damage and completely forgot her sins, and lived a happy life with her husband on the Shanghai beach for the rest of her life. Finally, when her husband carefully taught her to read, she understood love in addition to mountains, seas, and the sun. - From these places, we can recognize the playwright's ideological form, and there is no need to add any other explanations.

There is no doubt that the sadness, sorrow, and even anger of lost love here, and the psychological depiction of conscience condemnation, are highly cinematic, and successfully complete the success determined by the content. The director, whether in that section, whether it is the tone, or the atmosphere, all show William Keighley's mature skills. We are not very familiar with him, but here he does have amazing talent. Naturally, here we must explain that the mature skills of the playwright or the heroine very powerfully helped the director's success. In terms of the script, for example, he used a prisoner asking a stranger (Fang Shu went to jail to talk) for a cigarette, and used a thermometer to express Fang Shu's illness,... (there are countless examples) are very simple explanations of the story, and explain the surrounding environment. Rose's psychological expression is most obvious when she sees her rival's dog, and when she reads the news of the bandit's death sentence, and when she meets her husband for the first time after the murder. That excellent acting skill can be said to be unparalleled.

Unfortunately, this article cannot be written in more detail, other omissions.

Jinshan Shows His Skills in Jinshan Port

Jinshan switched from the stage to the screen. Because of his theatrical talent in the past, he took on the role of the male lead in Yueming Company's sound film "Madness" as his first voice on the screen. Yueming is currently shooting on location in Suzhou. The first filming location was Jinshan Port, and the first shot was Jinshan's scene, which can be said to be extremely coincidental. That shot was of Jinshan abducting his lover Wu Ling on horseback, with her sister Wu Lizhu protecting him from behind, but the enemy He Feiguang led his men to desperately chase after them. The gunshots were as dense as a string of pearls, and Jinshan took the lead, leaving the dust behind. Onlookers praised his good skills.

Prelude to "The Goddess"

— Nong

Being played with by people, being despised by society, under double oppression, a woman fights for her life.

In the arms of a man, she is a goddess, as filthy as dirt, trampled on by others, but in another context, she is a loving mother, as pure as the Virgin Mary, worthy of people's respect.

Contradictory life plunges her into extreme pain. However, society does not understand her. She endures all the ruthless scolding of the world and tolerates all the cruel insults, but in the end, she cannot protect her only beloved son.

Whose fault is this?

"The Goddess" is such a subject matter, handled by the emerging director Wu Yonggang, with an experienced set veteran joining the director's team. Even if it is a debut work, it will make people have absolute faith. (Que)

Evolution of the Wheel to be Released Soon

— Yun

Austin Motor Company Production Sound Film

"Evolution of the Wheel" is another new film produced by the British Austin Motor Company, following last year's sound film "Such Progress". The skill of its production and the brilliance of its content are even better than the previous film. The new film has now arrived here and will be released to the public at the Carlton Theater at 10:30 AM on the ninth of this month. All sectors are welcome to visit, and there is no charge. The new film is divided into: 1. Past and present view of the wheel. 2. Overview of the Austin General Factory. 3. Landscape film. 4. A glimpse of car climbing. The aforementioned three items are combined into five reels. The fourth item is a short film of two reels, titled "The Pinnacle of the World". Regarding the first section, the difference between the past and present wheels is always expressed by comparison. For example, the stagecoach, which was regarded as an important means of transportation in the past, is compared with the locomotive used for long-distance travel in recent times. The latter is agile and comfortable, while the former's driver sits proudly and ostentatiously parades through the city. Although it is also full of spirit, one can almost imagine that those who are in the car are not able to have a moment of comfort when they see its swaying and tilting state. Next, the 19th-century carriage and the early train with a high chimney are compared with the recently invented "Flying Scotsman" and long-distance electric sleeping cars in turn. The rate of speed is very different. At this point, the audience should feel the value of science even more, and need to catch up quickly. Regarding the second section, the overview of the general factory, how all the large and small parts of the Austin car are constructed and assembled is described in detail. The third section of the landscape film captures the scenery of various British villages and ancient buildings one by one, and the audience feels as if they are on the scene, and cannot help but feel relaxed and fascinated. As for the last two reels of short film, a glimpse of mountain climbing is the actual shooting of Austin "Seven" climbing the highest peak in Norway. All the processes are as if they are in sight. Rare scenery such as snow on the mountain peaks can also be fully enjoyed.

Film Novel

Mother-Daughter Affinity (Lady by Choice) (5)

— Zhong Jia

Alaban's beautiful eyes glanced around, and she couldn't help but be secretly surprised. She recognized Pansy as soon as she saw her. She walked straight up to Pansy and asked, "Haven't we met somewhere before?" Pansy smiled and pretended to have a southern accent, saying, "My dear, I don't think so. I have lived in Richmond, Virginia all my life... Not long ago, they invited me to live here for a while." After hearing this, Alaban couldn't help but secretly admire the old lady's acting skills, and remembered her roaring appearance in the midnight court that day, so she couldn't help but smile and said, "Then you must know Judge Daley, right?" Pansy also smiled back, winking at her, and slowly said, "Let me think... I know many noble people... Maybe I have met him." Alaban couldn't help but shout happily, "Okay, okay. Would you like to be my mother?"

That's how they made the deal. The news will also be published in the newspaper tomorrow. Johnny Mills seemed relieved when he saw the news, and sighed. Pansy had found a place to settle down. So he looked down and wrote a letter to Pansy to congratulate her. He felt that his responsibility was much lighter. On the other hand, after Paulaban brought Pansy home, she was happy all day long. She felt that Pansy was a very sensible person. She was very happy to buy clothes and so on for Paulaban, and she felt that it was worth it for the laughter Pansy gave her. The original plan she and Kendall had discussed was just to promote herself. But now, when Kendall occasionally mentioned their original plan and wanted Paulaban to send Pansy away, Paulaban became furious. But Pansy advised her instead, "Paulaban, what he said is not bad. I was originally a street wanderer, and I will go back to the street. And you don't have to worry, I will never say a word, saying that you took me out of the nursing home is just for publicity. I know you are a good person, and I will never hurt you." Paulaban reached out and shook hands with her, her voice with a sad tone, and said, "I know you are not afraid of anything, but I want you to stay here. May God bless your heart, I really liked you sincerely from the day you fought that salesman." Pansy asked in disbelief, "Really... Do you want me to stay here?" Paulaban said, "Of course it's true, don't worry." Pansy asked in disbelief, "Really... Do you want me to stay here?" Paulaban said, "Of course it's true, don't worry." Hearing this, Pansy cried with joy for a moment. Paulaban patted her back and comforted her, "Don't cry. I want you to laugh by keeping you here, why are you crying?" So they took out wine to celebrate their new collaboration. When Pansy raised her glass, her eyes couldn't help but contain a bag of tears, but she smiled with her mouth curved, "Congratulations on your happiness and fulfillment. All your actions are exactly the same as mine before." Paulaban looked at her, seemingly in disbelief, and said, "I'm afraid I can't compare to you."

Thus, their new friendship was built on respect and understanding, and it is rare for even true mothers and daughters to respect and love each other like that. Because Pansy deeply loved Paulaban, she had to protect all her interests. Therefore, she found out many of her manager Kendall's malpractices and places where he had deceived Paulaban. She told Paulaban and fired Kendall. From then on, Pansy began to plan for Paulaban, telling her to leave the humble life of the nightclub and become a true actress. Later, she borrowed some gambling money from Johnny Mills and went to the places she used to be familiar with, and won a lot of money back. She hired several famous teachers for Paulaban, teaching her singing, drama, and artistic dancing, all of which Pansy paid for herself. But she didn't dare to tell her where the money came from. She only said that a cousin of hers had died in Australia and left it to her, and Paulaban had to believe her. (To be continued)
